Then apply powdered vitriol to the wound after incision until the blood is staunched; then apply a poultice, and dress the place with dry things until it is clean.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there arises on the gums attached flesh which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore you must hold it with forceps and cut at its root, and let flow the bow or blood. Then apply powdered vitriol or other restrictive and drying powders to the wound; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it: for it will not return after the cautery. These are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gathered together at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scales which are ugly and harsh. And sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green and worms so that corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink. Therefore you must make the sick person sit between your hands, with their chin in your lap, and raise the teeth where the scales appear until there is nothing left; and thus do for the blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other stains, until they are clean; and if you remove what is at the first cause, it is good. If not, then begin again on the second day and the third until you have everything cleaned out. Know that teeth require various forms of instruments to clean according to what the work shows, for the instruments used to clean between teeth have different shapes than those used to clean around them; and these shapes and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating a toothache, you must delay extraction as long as possible, for it is not right to do otherwise; for this is a very high substance until one has no excuse for extracting.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained by thirst, you must be certain of the tooth that is aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain leaves the patient, and they believe it is in the wisdom tooth, and have the good tooth pulled. But still the pain does not depart by this means, for we have often seen this in such cases; and when you are certain of the aching tooth, then you must scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to guard the gum on all sides. Then move it slightly with your fingers or delicate pliers, bit by bit, until it is well loosened. Then firmly grasp it with the pliers. And hold the patient's head steady between your knees, so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take any of these instruments and put it gently on each side, and with the lever move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and wobbles, then you must fill it with wool where the hole is; and grasp it subtly with forceps so that it does not break when extracting; and there must be much bleeding around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And see to it that you do not break it, and if a piece remains, it will cause the patient greater pain due to the root's mischief.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeons who, out of haste and recklessness, sometimes break the jawbone and bring about what we have described; but they often cause serious illness through their carelessness in dealing with the roots left behind or the jawbone broken. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine, oil, and salt; and if bleeding continues, as it often does, sprinkle powdered vitriol on the spot; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one first moves the teeth should be long-pointed and thick-handled, so that they do not bend when extracting a tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large limbs so that they do not bend at all during traction, and let them be of iron well-made, and let them be toothed for holding movement.
de la racine des dens	Of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the draw, you must put moistened cotton smeared with butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the joint is softened, then insert the tweezers called "algefri", with which the head resembles a bird's beak; and they should be shaped inside like a file.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these pliers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called 'althali', that is, the crowbar, of which this is the shape:"
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	"And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root pops out because of this, that is good. If not, then help yourself with all the tools, of which the shapes come hereafter:"
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if one uses this tool that has two handles, of which this is the shape:"
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	"and other iron tools that are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this tool that resembles large pliers, of which this is the shape:"
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	"And let these tools be strong so that they cannot break, and know that there are many dental tools; and also other tools, which are not counted. Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	"And let them be thick and hold well to hold the bone so that it does not slip away but can hold and remove it; and then restore it with appropriate medicine for that place. Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	"When teeth appear not according to their natural position, and the shape is unsightly, especially in young girls, then you must know if the tooth is close behind the tooth, and not in its proper place, and it cannot be seen or filed. Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	"And tap the tooth lightly every day for several days to soften it and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent enough to be filed, then file it with such a file as this one has here its shape:"
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	"And it is also like the file used to make needles. And file the tooth lightly every day with this file so that it does not move too much until it falls out. Then plane the end with any smoother, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file down its sharpness enough so that it no longer cuts the tongue nor impairs speech."
quant li dent lochent	"When teeth lock"
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front of the joint becomes dislodged, either by injury or falling, and the patient cannot chew without causing pain, and you have tried medicine to tighten it but it is ineffective; then you must fasten it with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold does not change. And let the wire be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth. If you need to align the teeth, take the wire and wrap it double around the two healthy teeth first, then place the head between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side. Then start wrapping again up to where you started, and hold your hand gently and steadily so that it does not move; and let your knot be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot come loose.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the teeth of the string with a pair of pliers, and bring them together, and push them between the healthy tooth's roots, placing it so that it does not injure the tongue; then leave it tightly fitted as long as possible, and if it comes undone or the strings rotate, hold it fast with another string. It will remain thus throughout its time, forming the teeth and aligning the two healthy ones, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	"And when teeth fall out, if one replaces them in their place, gradually as we have said; and let not the foolish and impatient meddle with it. And sometimes they make the shape of a tooth from cow bone, and put it in the place where there is a gap, and hold it thus as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time."
de coper lou liien de la lengue	"To cure the tie of the tongue"
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never does this bond occur naturally at birth or by chance due to an old wound. Its treatment is as follows: open the patient's mouth and place their head in your hand, raise their tongue, then grasp and cut the frenulum from its base until the tongue is released from its attachment. If there is any scar tissue or callous, it is from an old wound, so insert a nail under it and cut through that bond as well. Be careful not to cut too deeply for fear of injuring the artery below. Once you have done this, rinse with rosewater and sage, or cold water, then place a linen pad underneath the tongue each night to prevent reattachment.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, grind vitriol and apply it to the spot; and if blood continues to flow, cauterize with a slow-acting cautery that is suitable for this purpose; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if you see it as of a livid or black color or hard and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre. And if it tends towards blenching and there is moisture present, use an onion and a sharp, fine spatula to scratch it open on both sides; and if bleeding occurs from your procedure, apply powdered vitriol until it stops flowing, then return to your procedure until all the furuncle is treated. Then rinse with sage and celandine, and treat it with other remedies until it is completely healed."
des apostemes de la gorge	Here is a translation of the text you provided about swollen glands in the neck:
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes, in the throat, bubbles called 'godath' appear; these are properly called tonsils. When treated as described in the division and they do not heal, beware: if it is a hard abscess with a small opening and dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for fear of bleeding; but let it ripen until it is ripe, then you can cut it open where it will break naturally. And if it is white with a small root, prepare the instrument to lance it, but first check if the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and his head in your hand, and he opens his mouth and takes the servant between his hands, and presses the tongue below with all the instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be made of silver or refined brass like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	"And when you press the tongue with the whole instrument and see the abscess, then take the awl and drive it into the amygdala. Then twist it upward as far as you can; wipe some lint with it, then cauterize with the instrument, which is shaped like a pair of tongs; but the ends are curved inward toward each other and very sharp. It is made of iron or bronze:"
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if you do not have this instrument at hand, cut it with pincers, which are shaped thus:"
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	"And it is sharp on one side and blunt on the other. And when you have cut one of the amygdalae, cut the other in the same manner, then after the incision, let the patient gargle with hot water and salt water, and if there is bleeding, let the patient gargle with water or decoctions of pomegranate peel or myrtle leaves, and similar things until the blood is stanched. Then treat it until it is healed. And sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two amygdalae, so cut them in the same way as the two amygdalae."
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was almost inside her throat, namely an abscess of small sense; and she had closed her throat so much that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had already risen so much that it had filled both passages of the throat with two raindrops each.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore acted quickly, and inserted a needle into one passage of the throat, then pulled it out and with it drew out a large portion of pus; afterwards I inserted another needle into the other passage of the throat, opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; then I inserted the needle into these abscesses and cut off part of them, from which only a little blood came out. And thus the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, but I did not stop cutting at this abscess for a long time; and it kept growing back, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large again. Then I excised and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it remained without growing any more; and I left these parts, and I do not know what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	"de l'uve"
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it comes down to the eye, and it is swollen and extended, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the swelling of the wound is soothed, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and that which is round gathered and not long; and it is sanguine or deep colored or black, then you must avoid incising it.

Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its blenching and lengthening, you must make the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then insert a needle into the eye, draw it underneath, and cut at the first two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two tendons.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. "And at the head there should be a hair, on which one puts the medicine, like the horse's tail of a spoonful, and places the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie on their side so that saliva and mucus run from their mouth away from the medicine towards it, so that it does not reach the throat or the belly. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it blackened and the biting of the medicine is calmed; and if you see fit, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with all the cotton in the cannus above until the cotton reaches the eye. "And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the head raised high. And make sure not to touch the epiglottis, lest the whole thing come loose, nor push the bone in; but rather let the patient put in the instrument themselves, for they will know where the thing is stuck. Then draw it out straight along the entire length of the instrument until it comes out completely."
de la sansue de la gorge	Here's a possible translation for "de la sansue de la gorge":
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet. Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye. Do this many times; it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is this: you take a pot that has live coals in it, and cover the pot with a cloth pierced in the middle, and place the head of the instrument through this hole. Then throw your fumigation onto it, and the patient puts the end of the tube into their mouth, closing the mouth so that no smoke escapes, but goes directly to the blood; and the blood will fall now, and if it does not fall, then begin the fumigation again many times. Let the patient suffer thirst, eat salty and stale foods, and do not drink water; then it will be necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	"And the shape of the instrument with which to treat the stone is like this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved forceps used for entering the throat; it should resemble the bill of a goose and have sharpness like that of a lime so that what it grasps, it cannot let go. See here its form:"
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter on Abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many sorts of abscesses are described hereafter in this book, according to the memories that come to mind, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two kinds of them, one being similar in appearance, and those that are moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the places where they occur on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and those on fatty tissue are different from those that come in joints; each has its own judgment in operation.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the bowel has completed its movement; and there are others that must be pierced when they have grown hard, even if they do not complete their maturation.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints and are left until they are completely surrounded by pus, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where an abscess is near the main member, and if you delay its perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the main member. Where it is near the fundament, pierce it before it dies. It is not necessary to pierce a hard abscess without digestion completed, except for one that is near the fundament which could rot inwardly and form a fistula; thus it cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you should know the time for performing an incision on an abscess that has fully ripened and burst: it is when pain eases, fever subsides, inflammation and redness diminish, and when the apex of the abscess becomes soft and pointed; and other signs. And it is necessary to perform the incision where the abscess hangs down most, or where it opens most; and the incision should be long, along the length of the body. If the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints near nerves and arteries, and in all smooth places without wrinkles."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where it pleases, according to this member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh, it is best that you delay their perforation until they are firm and digestion is complete, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this time, the body of the venom will spread out and be full of much filth; and sometimes its lips harden and its depth becomes difficult.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And some abscesses should be pierced according to the width of their body, according to what the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must bring small incisions, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out and cauterize; when they have become as hard as stones, and are mortified, then one must do likewise as with buboes: and there are such that are split into three angles, and there are such whose edges are cut like the leaves of myrtle, as angelic abscesses; and there are such where a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar cauterization.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, like superficial soft abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them plainly; and when the abscess is large, and it has filled much bowels, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the bowels at that hour, but draw out a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more again; do this many times gradually, until all the bowels come out; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying child, or young children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Because sometimes the spirit leaps with the release of the bowstring, causing the patient to die unexpectedly.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Be cautious then in this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, so open the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small. And if it is a full incision, bring linen or old cotton bandages; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, then you must place in each one a bandage so that they come together. And if you have cut off some skin from the abscess and have shaved around it, then you must fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth shreds without moisture, and bind it for three days; then open it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, bring cold water and a basin, wet a cloth in it, and place it on the bleeding area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blood continues to flow, you should apply treatment and care, using the powders I have mentioned in this book. If it is wintertime and the location of the boil is very nervous, then you must place moistened cloths heated with wine and oil on it; and if it is summertime and the location is fleshy, then you must place moistened cloths in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day. Then remove the dressing and cleanse and treat it as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	"And this one should universally know in the treatment of abscesses": I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is that chapter.
des soros	Here are some key points about boils (soros):
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	And small boils come from the head, and they are like those on hens' wattles, appearing in large numbers.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and moist like chickens; and there are others that are hard and bony when cut into, without any doubt that the artery opposes them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And this is how one performs the procedure of amputation: first, test all instruments called 'entromissoires', from which the form comes that follows, and what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	But if it contains moisture, then open it carefully over a long period.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And once the moisture is emptied, scrape carefully without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left behind; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, use water and salt to fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and these are the things that remain from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then begin again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure that none remains from the night; then dress the wound with suitable ointment, until it is clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is full of fat, cut it according to this form, carefully; then insert your tweezers and scrape from all sides, and focus all your efforts on drawing out the coat where it resides; and if the artery opposes you, do what I tell you later.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly, cauterize an abscess if it is hard, cut it open, and treat it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, since there is little blood involved.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And some of these abscesses have no moisture at their head, such as the ones I recorded on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone that could not be broken, so that if one had struck it, it would have made a wound like that from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming at the head, especially those that come at the heads of children and at the roots of ears, one should open them at their lowest point every day so that the bowels may issue forth, and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	"of scrofulas"
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and under the armpits, and among the anus, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and are interconnected.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each boil is properly inside its skin, like a pimple or a wound on the head, as we have said; and there are many kinds of these boils.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are evil ones that do not wish to obey healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Therefore, when you see one with a good appearance to the touch, and it is similar in color to the skin, moves from each side and is not hard near the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the vein, and is not deep; then you should cut it open on top, scrape away from each part, and draw apart the two edges of the heart once, if necessary, as we have said regarding head abscesses; and cut a little at a time, ensuring that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that the knife is neither too sharp nor too dull, so that your hand does not slip, and do not cut too deeply, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, then put powdered vitriol or some powders that stop blood into the wound, and press on the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased and the wound begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until you finish it; then check on your finger if there are any small scabs remaining, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, then do not cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong doubled thread and let it fall off without harm; then fill the wound with Egyptian oil-soaked cotton wool, then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scab, then it is necessary that you join the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that there remains no excess due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you must understand to cut the root of it, and draw out fire, and stitch as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold excessiveness, prick where it appears dead; and prick thus as the aforementioned one, depending on it, then bring tents with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, then treat it with ointment entering flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	de squinance could refer to "squinance" in Old French, which means "a kind of skin disease, scrofula".
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	"This is what the ancients said and spoke about the incision of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the record of their words."
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have strangulation, the epiglottis, which is called "epiglotte", must be avoided; and do not attempt aid through this method, for all the veins and the membrane of the patient are hot in the mouth or throat or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the membrane, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it below three circles or through a small cut across two circles, between the second and third cartilages, not in the cartilage; these are the places where the section of the epiglottis is made without flesh, and the vessels are long there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, he should extend the skin of the throat as far as possible, then cut towards the chin until it reaches it; avoid the blood vessels if you see any, and then cut the thyroidea membrane as we have said; this is demonstrated by the section of the thyroidea membrane that spurts fire where it is broken, and by the loss of voice; leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the critical hour has passed during which strangulation might occur, then bring together the two lips of the wound in the flesh and stitch it up without including the cartilage; afterward administer medicines that promote healing until it is whole again.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that this procedure should not be done unless the patient's throat is completely blocked and they are judged to be near death, otherwise there will be damage.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	**Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and dress it until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.**
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	**I saw that a young woman took the knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting part of the channel of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, but found her already dead.**
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and saw that blood had come out of it, and I knew that she had not cut her veins or arteries except for those in her throat, from which the windpipe was protruding through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	**I hastened and stitched the wound, dressing it until it was healed; but the young woman had only one fault, she was left hoarse of voice, and afterward returned to her state. Therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis there is no fear.**
de la grosse gorge	of a large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This bump is called "throat hernia", and it is a large bump with the color of a bruise, most common in women; it occurs in two ways: naturally, and accidentally; where the natural one has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one occurs in two ways: one is similar to a fatty lump, and the other resembles an arterial bruise; there is fear in this case, but one should only operate with fire on those that are small, and first prove and search with all the instruments: if you find it as big as one's fist, and not attached to any vein, cut it like you would a fatty lump, and remove its skin completely if necessary; examine everything carefully, and treat it appropriately until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	fatty tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many kinds of lumps exist, all of which I will describe their similarities; now I must say the whole difference between a lump and an ulcer.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is heat and fever lasting until the ebullition has passed, and corruption is completed; then fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the nodule there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains yellowish matter, which is its own fluid and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a cistern, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, either fatty or moist, and most of them are as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat dislocation, first examine and inquire about all the instruments called "intromittent" according to how their forms come in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiry into the apostemes of the nose is that you take the softest place that you find in the aposteme, and twist your fingers bit by bit until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the aposteme; then extract the foreign body, and beware of what comes out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture flows out, whatever its color, cut it like I said for other apostemes; and if no moisture comes after the foreign body, know that it is fatty, so cut it in cross shape, grasp it with forceps, lightly scrape each side, and guard the skin where it lies that you may draw it out intact with the nodule; and if you cannot draw it out intact, draw it out in pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If anything remains there, it returns again many times; and if a bit remains, and the blood becomes inflamed, then apply to the wound some corrosive waters, bind the wound, and place on it soothing hot poultices until it is healed. And if the inflammation is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and heal it with those that enter into flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beating is against you or another thing hastens itself and applies the powder of ground vitriol to the place, let it lie for two or three days until the wound purges itself and rests from ebullition of blood; then return to cut out what remains of the dislocation.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the shapes of the intruding instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small. There are three square ones called "albaret," and one called "breb." They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, for encircling fistular abscesses. They are also like the needles used to sew wounds, made of citrine bronze or iron or silver. Those that are yellow are most valued, but black ones are more commonly used to encircle fistular openings. They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of onions are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are onions that have two loops in three ways; and there are onions that have three loops, and they are also of three kinds; and there are onions that have two loops, and onions with one loop only, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these tools with which one cuts are sharp, and there are some that do not cut but from one side, for which reason one scrapes the skin off to avoid cutting the vein or nerve; and among these instruments are alembics placed in hands so that the patient does not perceive them when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are only used on thick flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar places; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling a fist's knuckles, according to this shape, with which one squeezes blood out.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is sometimes placed at the site where there is danger of cutting veins or arteries, and some are made in this large size:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never do the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like those of a woman; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them, let him do it according to this form from line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and dress the wound with healing herbs mixed with honey, then join the two lips of the wound together to sew them up, and let it heal until it is clean; and if the breast hangs down and is softened due to its size as happens in women, then cut it across into two parts above with two similar incisions; so that one touches the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from line .b. up to line .g.; then scrape off the skin between the two lips and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary for healing until it is clean; and if it is not clean, or the incision is not complete because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; leave it until it consumes the remaining fat, then heal it until it is clean.
des apostemes des asselles	"Boils in the armpits"
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"These boils that appear under the arms are hard, with knots, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	He who contains moisture must have the following form cut from the line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when all the matter inside the boil has been emptied out, then fill the wound with cotton wool and leave it until the following day, then remove all the cotton wool and dress it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed."
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	"If the boil resembles a scrofula, then incise it as we have said for scrofula incisions, and if the wound discharges matter, then apply a cautery as we have said before."
de la routure de l’artere	"Surgical procedure for arterial bleeding"
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is severed and the skin above it is closed, abscesses often form, and likewise when a vein is swollen with an abscess; and one can tell how this occurs by recognizing that if it's due to the artery, the abscess will be long and deep; but if you sense it with your fingers, it feels like a pulling sensation; and if it's due to the vein, the swelling appears prominent on the surface. It is foolish to cut into this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, at the angles, or around the neck, and in many other places, where it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the cautery of iron and likewise for the one who is at the head; also avoid cutting into one that has burst due to an arterial injury. Instead, cut along the length of the skin above the artery; then make an incision through the folds and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed. Then insert a needle underneath and pierce it through to the other side, and tie the artery with a doubled thread at two points, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples. Then prick the point between the two ties with an introductor until the blood comes out and the abscess is emptied. Then dress the wound as for an ordinary boil until it heals; but if the abscess is due to a vein incision, then take hold of what you can grasp of the skin around the abscess, then insert the needle underneath where you are holding, pierce it through, and tie it with a doubled thread so that you can draw it out from the other side. Then ligate the abscess as I have told you, tying the threads on either side at two points; but if you doubt that the threads may come loose, then insert another needle underneath all of the threads along the entire length of the abscess at the incision of the first needle and tie them at four points. Then cut into the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cut away the excess flesh and leave what is tied. Finally, place a warm compress soaked in wine and oil on it, then dress it with ointments and bandages until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	"Boils on the nerves"
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	"So boils can also occur on nerves when they are struck or from too much physical exertion and similar causes."
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often at the shoulders and hips, and in all places where there are joints. It is the most grievous abscesses, their color resembling that of the flesh, and they are in many dispositions without pain; but when pressed strongly, the patient feels pain, not deep within the body, but beneath the breast; it moves well in all directions but does not go forward or backward nor up or down. That which is in joints should not be cut with iron: there might be contraction thereupon. And those that are on the head or forehead make the skin rough at the scalp.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with tweezers and cut it at its root; but if it is large, suspend it with a hook and scrape it off, then remove the skin and sew the wound shut. Care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	"hanging pouches"
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in bellies and not elsewhere; it is an illness called 'fungus' because of its likeness. The roots are thin, the heads are large; some are small and others very large. I saw a man who had two on his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, with no difference between them. They were white, had a fine root, and were slightly split open, from which moisture constantly flowed.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found one weighing XVIII ounces, and the other VI З., and the work of the incision is such that you should look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is pale and moist with a subtle root; then cut it with a wide spatula, and have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	If there are many large blood flows during cutting, and if the blood overcomes you, then hurry with the cauterizer. But if the patient is frightened and afraid of the iron incision, take a well-made lead thread, tie it around the artelul as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and keep tightening the lead thread until it cuts the artelul without effort; and if the roots are large, be careful when cutting near the belly, but you can cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return. Then dress the wound, and make sure not to cut the thelul which is of fox color and poor sense.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an enchanted aposteme, and I will come to the cure of cancer hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a wound cautery or a fissure in the skin, and it is on the belly and in some cases of the beard, as happens with other eruptions, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries, according to what was said earlier, or from windiness; and if it is due to the eruption of the small intestine and the outlet of the gut, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and has diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the outlet of the intestines, then it is more diverse. And when you press it with your fingers, it rises up and then returns. And sometimes it is seized, and greatly enlarged at the entrance of the anus and by violent effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, without constraining; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess appears large and hard, and is fixed according to quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to touch, and its appearance indicates whether it is from arterial or venous blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.
