And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bladder, you must command the patient to tie his loincloth and lie down straight, then place a bolster around his belly. Then make him lie on his side between your hands, then go around the place where you have made the incision with the scalpel, then stretch half of the abscess up towards the greater trochanter. Then bind it around with a strong thread or silk cord tightly, and let the knot be free. Then open half of the abscess lying on the ligature, and put your index finger in and seek the intestine. If you find it caught by the ligature, untie it and put the intestine back into its place in the belly. And if you find the bladder, take it with pincers and cut off the excess. And if the artery or vein opposes you, go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads through them, and pierce the needles crosswise where you made the incision. Then hold the abscess in four places on the needles, and if it bleeds, remove the needles and leave the place until it closes by itself, and cut away the dead flesh when it becomes subtle and ripe. Then treat the area as necessary, and remove the abscess as we have said; then extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as necessary, and close the wound.
dou chancre	chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the appearances of a chancre and how one should operate with medicines, and how to avoid surgical cure. And we speak of an enlarging chancre in the marrow, and great caution is required in its treatment, and the ancients said that when chancres are in a place where they can be scraped away like those on the breast or hip, and similar places, one should remove it all at the beginning; but when it is large and old, one should not approach it, for I have never seen any healed nor has anyone before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is to purge the sick person with black colic several times; then make him sweat if there is visible swelling; then prepare the sick person one good day for the operation. Then grasp your tweezers or scalpel and cut around the chancre on all sides, and remove it completely without leaving any behind. And let the blood flow freely, then squeeze the wound with your hand or some other thing, and if bleeding from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then treat it with other dressings until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Regarding dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have previously discussed in the section the semblances of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each semblance, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is called only eclites; and one must not touch with iron in these two semblances: namely, tympanites and hipsparche, for they are deadly things.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharpened at both ends.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then thrust it in, but not so deeply that it can reach the intestine when it is inserted, and do not cause a cut; then look if the dropsy has entered near the intestines: thus you must make an incision of three fingers' width directly beneath on the right side; and if it is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the three fingers; and if it is due to worms, let it be on the right side, and it is not necessary that the patient lie upon the incision lest the superfluities run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with this tool, and insert it, and raise your hand with the spatumile between the skin and the syfac as in cutting a finger's width or around it; then pierce the syfac until the spatumile reaches the empty space, which is the place of water, then draw it forth, and into that tool insert this form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It is like a thin silver rod, and it is made of lead or light arrowhead material, and has one small hole at the tip; on one side there are three holes, two more on another side, and one on another; the head is cut like a feather, which is the form of the incision that writers use to trim feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, so when the instrument reaches the water, let it rest there. Then empty one third or half of it, for if you empty too much at that time, by chance the patient may die from the spirits leaving his weapon, or he may faint, or approach death. But empty according to its power and the indications of the patient's pulse and constitution. Then draw out the instrument and hold the water, which is retained by the heart closing the hole in the syphilis, as I have spoken about. Then you pierce according to this manner; then start the instrument again the next day if you see the patient enduring these things, and draw out a small quantity of water. Do this for several days, but guard against leaving too much water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much water there, cure it with a hot sepulture or sand bath, and often sweat or bathe in the sun, and cause him to drink; and cure it with drying medicines until it is dried up, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	"Regarding the obstruction of the instrument"
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without any opening in their penis, or with a small opening, or one that is not in the correct place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it needs to be done immediately, pierce it with a very fine spatula according to this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place the thin lead plug in the hole and tie it, holding it like this for three or four days. When he wants to urinate, remove the plug, let him urinate, and then replace it. And sometimes it may not be necessary, because the urine coming out will not leave the hole closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small, let him apply clay of lead, as we have said; it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	He who does not have the wound in its place is burned, for some are born with the wound at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because semen cannot reach the mouth of the urethra, and this is a bad condition.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And the manner of performing this operation is that the patient lies on their back, then extend the tip of the penis and cut it like the tail of a feather so that the hole falls in the middle as it should. And be careful not to cause bleeding, which happens frequently, and if it does happen, stop the bleeding with whatever stops bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed."
des pustules de la verge	"Regarding the pustules of the penis:"
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Many times these swellings appear on the penis, which is an ugly appearance of flesh. There are some that are malignant and others that are not. You must take them with a sharp needle and cut them out and clean them all, then place moistened cotton in Egyptian ointment on them; then treat them with diafinicon ointment until they are healed."
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is malignant, foul-colored and foul-smelling, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it out, and if the wound is on top of the penis, with part inside the skin and part outside, then first remove the part that is inside; and when it is healed, then treat the outer part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if you treat it all together, the head of the penis may not be completely healed and blackness and corruption will come to his penis and testicles; so everything that is black and corrupted must be removed, then apply a plaster made from pomegranate peel and honey and flour, and then treat it with other remedies until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding starts, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And the cauteries help with two conditions together: namely, for bleeding and corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you should insert or guide into it a tube of lead, so that the patient can urinate through it. And when the skin around the head of the penis is hard due to inflammation which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or due to a wound or abscess, then you must cauterize with the hair remover until the liens are untied and the head of the penis is released from all sides. And if it's difficult to separate them, then you should cauterize with the spatula slightly on the head of the penis and skin; then carefully cut between them, and put a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water there, so that it may soften again.
de la circoncision	"Regarding circumcision:"
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	"Circumcision is not the removal of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this operation by choice and especially on children, it is necessary that we do our best to make it the best and easiest operation for healing."
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	"I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience."
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	"For I have wanted the majority of masters and surgeons who perform circumcision to use a single clasp, and forceps, and a novacula; thus it was easy for the heart because there are two layers, and sometimes one cuts the top one and leaves the bottom one."
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	"Or the circumcision is double pain, and at the cleansing of the glans the point of the member is not secure; and in the cleansing of the foreskin sometimes the iron slips away and mars the work, and many times it happens that they do not need cleansing and I have seen this."
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	"Regarding the cleansing that is done with forceps along the entire length of the thread, I have found through experience that it is good because forceps cut equally well above and below."
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, cut evenly in one single stroke; but ensure the thread is tightly wrapped around the skin. The manner of the first operation should be such that you make the child understand, if he hears, that you are only tying the thread around the stick, and then allow him to enjoy all possible ways; then hold him upright between your hands, and hide the forceps between your hands or under your feet so the child does not see them, nor any instruments. Then insert your hand up to the stick and blow into the heart, pulling it upwards until the head of the stick is inside. Then clean it well from the dirt that has accumulated there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie below at another knot; hold it with two fingers by the second knot near the wrist and thumb, and cut between the two knots, then quickly lift the heart upwards and pull out the head of the stick. Then let the blood flow freely from vein to vein, for this is what moistens; then place powder on it and on the powder a gauze glued with an egg yolk cooked undiluted with rose water, compounded with good rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and continue the treatment until he is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	"The shape of the weights for purification should be this: the two heads should be thin and sharp; they should also be as large as a hazelnut each."
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	"The error of purification is when the heart within slips during incision; therefore, you must extend it with your finger before the wound becomes inflamed; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, use tongs to do so."
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	"And if it takes three days and what is under the shaft is swollen, then leave it until the inflammation has subsided, and lightly scrape away the scab; cut as much as you can move without hurting yourself, but be careful not to damage the part of the shaft, for it will not harm him at all."
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"So treat the wound with healing powder as we have said when speaking of powders. If you cut too much and it goes upwards, it will not harm him. Treat it as we have said until it is completely healed."
dou retenement de l’urine	"On the retention of urine"
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by stone, or frozen blood, or bowel, or flesh born, or similar things, which we have discussed in the division. And if the urine is not released, and you see that the obstruction is due to a stone located at the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be made to bend over his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and let the patient lean back as much as he can. Then the neck of the bladder will be forced open for the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released. And if it does not come forth, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction using all the instruments called "syringe", of which this is the shape: and it should be made of thin, light silver, like the feather of a bird; and its tube should be one-and-a-half palms long, and fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of issuing urine is thus: you take a doubled thread, and tie at the head one pouch of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; then cut off the excess wool and place it up to the head of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forward until it touches the bladder, and when the patient feels this, then pull out the thread along with the wool pouch by pouch, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and make the urine flow; and repeat the syringe process until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Here are some examples of what "des maladies de la vessie" might mean in English:
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When the skin is peeled off and blood flows into the bladder, or putrefaction has gathered there, and you see that water and medications are being distilled from it, then use all the instruments called "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see. The raised place is such that the medicine can be inserted tightly without addition, so that moisture can be drawn out, and introduced when necessary; and when you want to introduce your medicines into the bladder, put the tip of the syringe in the moisture, and draw the tube that is inside; then draw the moisture into the syringe, and then push the tube back in firmly; thus the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one irrigates the bladder.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher. Below there are two openings, one on each side where the rope hangs down. Then take a sheep's bladder and put into it the moisture with which you wish to irrigate the bladder. Then tie it firmly between the two breasts with a good doubled thread, and warm this moisture over the fire for a short time. Then insert the tip of the enema into the tube, then press your hand firmly on the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder. And if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a round circle out of it, and pierce it evenly around. Then insert the thread firmly through these holes, then gather the circle together as one gathers a net, and put within this what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument. And do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	"de la pierre"
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	"We have already said in the section on stones and their extraction together with medicines; and we have explained the difference between stones engrained in the kidneys and all the signs, and in which stones one should operate by cutting; and in the bladder and in the penis; and I will tell you this clearly and briefly."
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	"I say that stones engrained in the bladder happen more often to children, and this is a sign that water flows from the bladder like water in its subtlety. And they perceive sand there, and the patient grasps his penis, and he feels many times, and then it hardens; and many times these are the foundation of pain. And the cure for children is easy until they are four years old, and it is very difficult for the elderly, and it is average for young people, those who are between youth and old age. And the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones."
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with a clyster, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes obstructs seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, tilt them and move them downward so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it may rise to a high place; then have him sit between your hands, and his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely tilted downwards; then search for it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in its space, quickly cut towards the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall upon touching it all around, then moisten your right index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is a fully grown youth; and insert it into his fundament, seek out the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press down on your finger and push the stone towards the opening where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	"And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch his right hand up towards the scrotum, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the scrotum in the part where the incision is made. Then insert the spatula shaped like this:"
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	**And make between those that are between the thighs and the fundament, not in the middle but at the side of the left thigh; and it should be straight on the stone, and your two hands should always be on the fundament, and the cut of the traverse should be so that it is wide by default, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure will cause the two that are on the fundament to jump out without labor; and know that there are such stones that have angles and edges: they are difficult to pass; and there are those that are smooth, like a pebble, and rounded, from which the exit is easy.**
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	**Therefore, for those that have angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not jump out, then you must extract with forceps which are also like a file at the head, so that you can grasp the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under it a subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot grasp it thus, then widen the small hole in the opening, and if blood flows out, then stop it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first place the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then let them flow out, and then the others if there are many.**
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be so, and a larger wound must be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And there are two things that can happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine begins to flow from where the wound cannot heal. But nevertheless, strive to pull it out with forceps, or cut it out with pincers, piece by piece; and once you have completed your task, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, then bandage it tightly, and place a wet cloth dipped in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water on top, to cool the hot abscess. Then bind the patient around his neck, and do not untie the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when you untie it, then wash the area very well with oil and water, then dress it with diapheconointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed."
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and corrosions appear in the wound, and blood clots form in the bladder, causing urine to be retained and come out without warning with urine: then boil your thumb in the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder. Then wash the wound with water, honey, and salt, and help the patient in all ways that you know until he is healed. And every time you treat him, you must bind both his thighs together, and apply medicine to the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it lies in the passage of the penis and it's stuck there and urine cannot come out; then perform the treatment I mentioned earlier, cutting many times until it's freed from this cut.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	"Take one iron rod according to this shape and let it be forked at three ends stuck into one stick:"
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the trocar into the penis gently until it reaches the stone; then turn the trocar in your hand against the stone a little at a time until you can pierce the stone on the other side; then urine will soon flow, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if it breaks quickly and comes out with the urine, then the patient is healed. And if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders it, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then make an incision in the penis at the location of the stone between the two threads, then remove it and untie the thread, and clean the wound with cold water, and treat it until it's healthy.
de la piere des femmes	"from the stone of women"
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	"It happens rarely that a stone becomes lodged in women, and if it does happen, its treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-versed who reveals herself to doctors, especially when she is chaste."
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	**And the third manner is thus: On occasion one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; And the fourth manner is thus: The stone of the woman is more deeply situated than that of man, therefore one must make a deeper cut there, and great fear exists. And if you need such help, then you must take a skilled midwife, and barely can one find her, and if you do not find one, then seek a subtle caster; And present him with a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her to perform what you command concerning the inquiry into the stone; And examine very well whether the woman is virgin: Then she must put her thumb on the fundament and seek the stone; And if she finds it, then press it down with her thumb, and recommend that she put her thumb in the vulva of the patient, and feel and press her left hand strongly on the bladder.**
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut against the stone in the root of the thigh near the middle of the groin where it has moved into position, and feel for the stone in that area; and do not move your knife above or below the stone, making the first incision small; then insert the knife into the incision if you feel the stone so close to the wound that the stone can come out forth, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	and know the similitudes to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood vanquishes you, then place powdered vitriol on the wound, and let it stay there for an hour until the blood stops flowing; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have with you the instruments that I told you about in extracting stones from men to aid you in your work; and if the blood vanquishes you again, and it is from the artery that was cut, then place powder on the wound and bind it tightly with cloths and bandages, do not begin cutting again, and leave the stone alone without attempting to remove it, lest by chance the patient die; then dress the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	"And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wound is healed, then return to your task until the stone is out."
de hernie carnouse	Hernia carnosum
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	"Pus ouse n'est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l'uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l'uef, si c'on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c'est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nous avons dit; et ceu n'avient se poc non."
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	"And the generation of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the intestines, and this matter is spread out."
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it occurs due to percussion on the joints; this moisture has many colors: either declining towards jaundice, or without redness, or black, or whitish and watery, which happens more often. These are signs of recognizing such a gathering, for if it is sac-like white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, about the size of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper skin, then the abscess is ripe with a portion of the egg-white, and therefore it is thought to be another egg; but if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the sac-like white, one feels it well. Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, squeeze the entire contents into a square glass, as shown above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	"So according to what comes after the probe, judge what is inside."
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we operate with iron (i.e., cauterize), the patient must be in good health according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then have him lie on his back, upon something a little high, and put many cloths underneath him. Then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the joint of the heart. Then take the spatula lightly, and cut the skin of the joints among the long hairs down to the flesh, and let your incision be straight, dividing the skin of the joints up to the sac-like white, and scratch it subtly according to your strength; then pierce the sac full of water with a large hole, and extract all the water, and then put on your bandages, and stretch the sac upwards. And do not touch the joint of the heart, but only the sac; cut everything away or in pieces subtly from it, that if you do not cut it well, the water will return. And if the egg should fall out during your operation, put it back in its place when you have finished the operation on the sac. Then sew up the two leaves of the joint of the heart with a suture, then cure it as other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	"And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to ligate the vessels that are suspended there, preventing bleeding; then cut the intestines along their entire length and remove the egg, and heal it as we have said."
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if water is gathered in two parts together, knowing that these are two branches; cut the other part equally as you did the first one, then squeeze out the blood, and put clean linen moistened with rose oil on the wound; and place another piece of linen moistened in wine and oil over both wounds, and cover them with doubled cloths, and bind it all according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with wool wadding according to this form and sew them together at the waist of the breeches, and one of the heads should be placed on the buttocks up to the back, and the other at the wrist area; and the other two ends are placed over the two angles, and all the restraint should be assembled in the loop of the breeches. And sometimes this branch is medicated with cautery instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take one subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the wounds, and heat it as we have said, so that the white spongy substance containing water is exposed; then take the cautery in this form, and pierce that sponge with incisions, and burn it with this subtle hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And prune it in all ways that you can, until you strip it bare; and ensure that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more sound; and move carefully to avoid bleeding, and moisturize the cut surfaces; and if anything goes contrary to you, whether a boil bursts or bleeding occurs or some other thing, then treat what goes contrary to you, according to what is said beforehand.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to endure this procedure due to its horrifying nature, then prepare for perforation, as I instruct you. And when you are certain through the signs that we have said that running water is present, then seat the patient on a raised chair; pierce the boil at its lower part with a wide spatula, and insert the perforation tool along the length of the body; make the opening large enough so that all the water flows freely. Then place cotton on the site and tie it, allowing the remaining water to flow out, then treat until the wound is healed. And if the white cloth does not allow the water to exit from the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument used for treating hydrocele, whose form is shown beforehand. Widen the opening of the wound, and know that the water returns, assembling again after six months or thereabouts. And when it assembles as before, so shall the patient pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the boil on the buttocks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this vein there is fear and many dispositions [positions], therefore it seems to me that it would be better if one leaves it alone; and I will tell you about its workings and similar things regarding the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	"I say therefore that many boils come on the body, and especially on the intestines; and this happens in many cases."
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known that this abscess comes from an acid and sharp humoral imbalance, spread through the joints or caused by injury; its color matches that of the body's skin; it causes no pain but is serious nonetheless. Sometimes there are multiple abscesses that are pale and red, with a foul smell, which can also come from an arterial issue or venous inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it can be recognized by the hot and hard nature of the abscess when pressed between two fingers; you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	An abscess caused by venous inflammation is recognized by its softness upon touching with two fingers; you can safely make an incision here and on other similar areas. First, cut around the edges of the joint, then raise the skin upwards, expose the white fat beneath, and remove the suspending ligament from all sides of the egg [ovary].
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hard with these new-born chicks, then you must pull out the egg and the chick; and if it is aired on the shaf or in the one that is inside the vessels, then you must remove all of this tension, and round off the chick.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the origin of the flesh is at the back, you must cut it all away, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your operations are complete, apply linen soaked in rose oil and wine to the wound, then dress it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the boil on the buttocks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a tumor covered by a growth resembling a boil, with softening of the flesh, and the patient cries out when touched; and the treatment for this illness is almost as frightening as the one mentioned before, nevertheless we will tell you its workings according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must have the patient sit on an elevated seat, then hang the suspensory ligaments of the testes down onto your two fingers, close to the penis, and tie them with a thread, stretching them out well. Then cut through the skin over the vessels with a broad, sharp scalpel, exposing them, and then scrape away from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries from the temples. Then insert a needle with a double thread where the vein emerged first, and tie it at the first point where the vein appeared, and tie it again at the other end. Then cut through the middle correctly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moistures. Then dress the wound as you would others where a bow is inserted, so that no vessel falls which nourishes one of the testicles; for by this there comes no harm, and if there is veining in all the vessels, then you must draw the testicles from all the vessels, so that the scrotum does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they become dry and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the nose
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this disease occur through the division that comes from the bladder, or the stretching over the abdomen in the angle region, because of which the intestines descend from that breach to one of the hips; and this breach is either from the bladder or from the stretching of it, and these two types come from many causes: such as a fall, a leap, a blow, lifting heavy weights, and similar things; and the sign when it's from the stretching of the bladder, is that it happens gradually over a long time, and does not happen suddenly; and the abscess is even up to its depth, because the bladder presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign when it is a cut in the thigh is that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and there are various visible swellings under the skin, which is due to the leakage of intestines and blood from the wound in the thigh
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	Sometimes the rings are torn along with the intestines, which are retained inside and cause great suffering for the sick person, especially when they are pressed upon
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of iron wounds, it is necessary to avoid them
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	The manner of this operation is that you command the patient to insert their intestines with their hand into the wound if it can be reached; then press on their neck between your hands and lift their hips; then stretch out the heart above and cut all the skin from the long hip bones; then insert the scissors of the waist's ring according to what you need to open the wound, and let them be such that the bone can come out; then peel back the bladder which is underneath the skin of the hip bones until the white hard bladder is exposed on all sides; then put your right index finger into that which leads to the hip bone, in that which is between the white bladder which is under the skin of the testicle and between the second bladder, and separate that which is behind the testicle and between the second bladder; and then move with your right hand inside the hip bones and stretch out the white bladder upwards with your left hand, and lift the testicle together with all the bladder towards the waist; and command the assistant to stretch out the testicle upwards and loosen that which is against behind the attachment; and search with your two hands if there is any intestine wrapped around the hard white bladder, and if you find anything, put it back into the abdomen underneath; then take a needle which has one thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it in the rear part of the bladder which is after the hip bones, after the waist, then cut the heads that appear from the threads until there are four threads; then tie them together in the manner of a cross, and tie the bladder with it, as we have said before, with a strong tie of two parts; then wrap the heads of the threads and tie them firmly with two ties so that no vessels which nourish it can enter there where pus may come; and put back the tie according to the first tie long two fingers from it, and after these two ties leave some of the bladder which is underneath the hip bones in the palm of your hand; and after everything else according to the roundness that the testicle carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the hip bones until the blood flows out, and the bowel as we have said before; then bring moistened wool in oil and put it on the wounds, and bring the tie that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes cauterize the white flesh that we have mentioned after the incision, for fear of bleeding
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times and let the lien fall through it; and if it delays in falling, then raise with hot water, and put on what we have said until it falls; then treat the wound with another treatment until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Hernia carnosum
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I never saw anyone daring to perform the cure by iron
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch which is together with the vise, in such a manner that you tie the vessels after the incision, lightly below upwards; then cut into it, and treat the abscess from what opens until the vessels fall; and cure it as we have said until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin as we have said, and opens up the site; and let no part of the intestines slip out through the wound, and if some do slip out it is little matter, and repair them at once; but even so if it remains too long in this state the wound becomes inflamed or syphacated until the intestines slip out; and this happens by the extension of the syphac which is in the groin as we have said, for it stretches then softens and swells the site opens up; and its cure is by cautery as we have before said; but sometimes it is cured by iron in this way: And let the patient lie often on his back between your hands, then cut into the swollen site of the rupture with a width according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the syphac which is under the skin that is affected, then take the reed and place it over the opening of the syphac; and press it firmly down on the lower abdomen, then sew up both openings of the syphac upon the head of the reed, sewing each one separately; then extract the head of the reed, and do not cut into the syphac or extend the wound or anything else, as I have taught you in the cure of the rupture of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and dress the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sinew is contracted and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is more effective at this point and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Regarding the softening of the skin around the anus
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the anus in some men becomes softened due to the softening of the flesh that is inside, and it is unpleasant to see. And when one wants to treat it, let the patient lie on his back, and cut away the softened skin from the natural skin. Then join the two lips together with a single stitch, and if you wish, sew up the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches. Then cut between the stitches and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the threads.
dou chastrement	Regarding castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	And know that castration is forbidden by our law, and therefore I would not wish to speak of it in this book; however, there are two reasons why some information about it may be necessary: one is so that the physician can respond when asked about it and its treatment; and the other is because we often have need of the castration of certain beasts to aid us, such as of goats and sheep and dogs and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method that we use traction, make the beast sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then grasp them with your hand so that they are replaced and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For castration by cutting: you must restrain the beast, and press the skin of the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspensiony ligament, and cut each testicle once after you have well scraped them; leave a little bit of the sheath and the subtle sheath that is over the vessels; and this method of castration is safer than that done by traction, because in traction some part of the testicles may remain, causing the beast to desire lust; then dress the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Regarding hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermafroditism comes in two ways among men: one way is that between the two testicles opens also like the figure of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes it leaks urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, who have on their pubic region both a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is that you cut away all the attached skin and treat it like other wounds; in the second manner, for those men whose urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	Regarding hemorrhoids：
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is an attached skin on the natural part, as long as it is too unsightly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you shave the excess skin of the tentigene with your hand or with scissors, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep lest blood flow, then treat the wound with other remedies until it heals. And there is another skin that grows at the mouth of the womb, and the anus, and sometimes jumps out furiously, and resembles a cow's disease, which is why the ancients called it "cow's illness".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must cut it, as we have said regarding the tenting procedure, and care for it until it is healthy.
de erratique	Of the erratic
