Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	An error is when the nature of the woman's body is not pierced, or if the opening is small; it is either natural from birth, or accidental due to illness that has occurred there; or it is caused by tissue joined together, either thin or thick skin, and is located deep in the womb, or on the sides, below, or wherever it may be; it prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes the flow of menstrual blood; and its recognition comes from examining the vulva.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is near the surface, then search with your fingers or a probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is thin skin and close to the surface, then hurry up and do this: put your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then press the two lips firmly until the thin skin is taut and covers the swelling; then take linen, moistened in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman rest each day so that it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the shoulder blade is hard and thick, you must shave it like a laurel leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is flesh-born, suspend it with a plaster and shave it; and have medicines that stop blood flow, such as aloe, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white. Then apply a wide cloth bandage so that the wound cannot heal. And do this repeatedly until it is healed. Then dress it with other remedies until it is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh comes out in the wound, it must be shaved in this manner, unless it's an inflamed abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the inflamed abscess that is in the wound, one should not apply fire.
des emorroides	**Hemorrhoids:** Hemorrhoids are varicose veins inside or outside the anus; they appear as small lumps like bunches of grapes; some are internal and invisible from without, while others are external; they cause pain when defecating or sitting down; they can cause blood to flow freely during defecation or after, or only stain the toilet paper; sometimes they prolapse and come out at defecation; they are caused by constipation due to a bad diet, heavy lifting, or frequent diarrhea. The cure for them is to avoid their causes: eat healthy food that does not cause constipation, drink plenty of water, exercise regularly, do not lift heavy objects unnecessarily, and use ointments to relieve pain and inflammation. For internal hemorrhoids, surgery may be necessary if they are large or causing significant symptoms. Otherwise, rubber band ligation, sclerotherapy, or infrared coagulation can be used to treat them. For external hemorrhoids, warm sitz baths, witch hazel pads, and over-the-counter creams can provide relief. In severe cases, surgery may be necessary.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are the openings of veins which usually do not bleed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; and we have already spoken in the division about their similarities, signs, and now I will say those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are deeply embedded in the flesh, and are not visible to the touch, then iron treatment is not applicable.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the anus, which one can feel, those are the ones that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must place the woman in a cold house, then stretch open the mouth of the anus with forceps, grasp it with the pincers at its root, then sprinkle medicinal powders that constrain blood flow, such as acacia and dragon's blood and frankincense and similar substances; then hold her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water. If bleeding starts, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gall nuts and similar things. Then take barley flour, mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without injuring; then take linen, and soak it in plantain juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply to the location.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the boil is ripe, apply ointment to the location until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a bitter apple, so it must be cut as I have said before; and then care for it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	**Abscesses of the Rectum:** Abscesses of the rectum are localized collections of pus that can develop due to infection or injury to the tissues of the anorectal area. Symptoms may include pain, swelling, redness, warmth, and fever. Treatment typically involves incision and drainage of the abscess under local anesthesia to relieve pressure and allow the pus to drain out. This procedure is usually performed by a surgeon or colorectal specialist. If the abscess is deep-seated or associated with significant inflammation, the patient may require intravenous antibiotics to fight infection and prevent it from spreading. In some cases, a seton (a loop of suture material) may be placed into the abscess cavity to allow for ongoing drainage over time. It's important to note that untreated abscesses can rupture spontaneously, causing severe pain and potentially leading to serious complications such as sepsis or fistula formation. Therefore, prompt medical attention is crucial for proper diagnosis and treatment.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of boils come in the flesh, such as cancer and stone boil, herpes and erysipelas and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot boil, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must discuss in this treatise the hot boil that comes on the flesh, which is not one of those boils that grow over; and if you wish to know how to work with iron, look first whether the boil is full at its beginning, hot and feverish, and turns red when viewed.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not rush to pierce [the skin], but make the hole so large that the pain is appeased. Then seat the patient on a chair, with two small chairs where they can lean back and support their back and assemble their feet against the thigh; and let their thighs be spread wide, and place their arms under their knees, and bind them tightly with a good binding. Then suck the bag towards the right side, and bring forth the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the marrow, whose form comes later; and it is necessary that when you prepare this instrument, you first insert the rod to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient. And if the instrument is too large, then cover the depth of the marrow with rags, so that the instrument does not hurt. And it is necessary that they place the funnel of the instrument above, and wet the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and it is cut with a gentle hand, then it is necessary to cover it at the head, at the spatula's edge; and when the bowels are empty, then you must place in the wound wet bandages in rose oil or dry green oil; and put the bandage far from the wound at the bottom of the marrow, and put behind it on the marrow and on the linen cloth well-washed in water where mallow is cooked; then after two days of suitable ointment, until it is healed; and sometimes they lift the marrow and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then with water where lily roots and long coltsfoot are cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is located in the marrow, then you must refrain from cauterizing with fire, but treat it as we have said in the section on dislocations.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first that the midwife knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the sign is when you see the woman hurry forward, and desires to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out forthwith; then know thou that this birth is according to nature's figure, and the afterbirth is under its head, and the secondine with it; and when thou seest these signs, then press her belly gently so that the child comes forth quickly; for when it descends upon its head, then is the secondine with it, and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities by good cleansing; and he who comes otherwise comes not naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes upon its feet, and the body or head comes forth first, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, sometimes, and is turned perhaps upon its neck, and in other evil figures; therefore it is necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in these things, and guard against error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes forth naturally upon its head and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a stool or let women hold her up; and raise her nature with oil of almonds or fennel cooked, and then place the midwife between her thighs the little spatula, whose form is as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and break the amniotic sac, and cut with its nail until the moisture inside comes out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then one must administer a clyster to the woman made of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil; then let her sneeze and yawn, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out first, then you must gently push them back bit by bit; and if they cannot be put back in, then place the woman on a seat, and raise her feet up high; then tilt the seat towards the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the tilting; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the joint that is mentioned here, and extract the child, and realign it properly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the delivery of a child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, one must place it upright; then turn it gently and gently until it is even; then take one foot and stretch it gently
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the hips, order it to grasp, and make it sneeze with condition; then jump forth if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if there is no cautery as we have said, then it should be turned little by little until it matches its natural shape
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it becomes easy
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take musk in old wine and oil of sesame, and melted gum, grind all together in one mortar; put this ointment on the woman's nature and let her sit in warm water up to below the ribs; and when she is moistened below, place a collar of myrrh around her and put it beneath her, leaving it for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for now the child will leap forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	"of the child's exit onto its knees"
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child arrives in this form, then let the midwife place her hands softly and gently; then support him on his neck, and let his feet hang down, and let him lie on the bed; and fold his hands softly and gently, and then place his hands on his belly, and remove the cushions from below, so that he may be positioned correctly. And if the child does not slip out, then take his feet and move them forcefully, then move his belly upwards, then place your hands there; and wipe the child softly and gently; and instruct the woman to press down until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	"One hand comes out during the birth of the child"
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	If you cannot bring the hand back into position: if she cannot be brought up, then make the woman get up and walk around; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, and forcefully raise her legs; then apply the muscilage that I have described; and if she does not give birth, then seat her on a chair, and study how to bring the hand back into position; and wipe the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, and tell her to press down until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	"At the moment of birth, with its hands spread wide, facing its mother's back."
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient grasp their hand, then turn it gradually and gently; and when it is even, so place on it the musky nature of althea and oil, as we have said, then tell them to move it gradually; and when you have done this, let her sit on the seat, and tell her to sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	"This same manner is used for the afterbirth."
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When heat comes upon the amniotic sac in this manner throughout the secondine, then cut the amniotic sac with your thumbnail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child lies on its face and neck, then cut it from behind so that it is not retained, and the child dies. Then put the child inside until you have placed it correctly, and tell the woman to push a few times: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	"Regarding the birth of twins:"
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	"It is well known that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or even four; this is not a strange thing and happens infrequently."
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if they have no name; I know these ones, which multiply, and are desired by the syphac who devours them, which is attached to the navel; and sometimes they come out naturally just like a tooth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out crying, treat them as we have said, and let the physician be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does; and do thus as it is worth moving for health.
de plusors enfans	"Regarding multiple births:"
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb with one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or even more, and all are formed into the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise physician's glory. And it is necessary for the physician to know all this, for similar things have happened before; so act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	Regarding a stillborn child:
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	And when you treat the woman with the dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained by necessity to act with your hands; then you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fears death. Then the woman should be propped up on her back, with her hips inclined downwards and her legs raised. And the assistant should tie her thighs with two cloths, or she should be tied to the bed so that she is not treated while descending the child. Then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with althea and fenugreek and linseed. Then the physician should anoint his hands with these oils and muscillaages. Then insert them into the womb gently, then move to where it fits best for the child to descend on its head. And make sure the child is properly positioned before inserting the hook in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or near the navel or near the sides. If the descent is on its feet, insert the hook or crochet and into the middle of the sides. And it is necessary to hold the hook in your right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of your left hand, and insert it gently with all your hand, and insert the hook into any of these places that we have said until the thing is empty.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then stick one against the other, or use three if necessary, so that the extraction is even; then stretch them evenly by moving from one side to the other, so that movement comes out, and let the forceps' teeth grip for holding.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some part remains, then smear some of its dough with oil and place the hands in that part, and pull the other part; and if none remains, then place this forceps higher up and do so until all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be pulled back due to tension, then you must wrap it with a cloth until all comes out; then cut at the joint of the sole or at the elbow, and do likewise for the other hand.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and tight at the opening, or has a sharp point assembled on top, then you must place the spatula spinous between your hands, split open the top, and remove the pointed bone; or you can round it with the tool called 'almidach,' whose shape comes with the tools in the chapter that follows this one; and do likewise if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head does not come out despite being pulled strongly, cut it open until the moisture at the foot of the opening comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it piece by piece as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce there until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	"And if the child is on its feet, traction will be light, and the alignment of the mouth of the marrow will be easy."
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or breast, then you must draw it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut into the belly or breast until the moisture that is there escapes; and if the other members are removed but the head remains, then place your hand deep into the marrow, and pull until you reach the mouth of the marrow; then insert one or two fingers, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed there, then you must not work there, rather moisten it with moist and fatty substances; and apply plasters, and soak in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is lying on its side and you cannot make it lie flat, then treat it as we have said for a living child; and if one cannot do so, then pull it out piece by piece, and leave no part of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And once you have done this, if the patient suffers from abscesses as we have mentioned that come on the skin, and if there is an outflow of blood, then it should be placed in hot water that has been restrained, and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	"I saw a woman whose child had been bitten in the abdomen by one mouse, then another mouse came and bit the other."
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	"After many days, an abscess formed on her cheekbone and swelled so much that it opened up, causing great pain."
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	"I was called to treat her, but after thinking about it for some time, I could not heal the wound."
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	"I applied a poultice with strong drawing power and out came one bone, then after a few days another."
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	"I was greatly amazed at this because the abdomen has no bones."
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	"So I thought it must be the bones of a dead fetus."
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I sought the wound, and drew out many bones until the woman was much better. And the woman lived for a long time like this, and sometimes a little bowels came out from there; and I recorded this chapter because whenever the master finds something strange, he knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	"on bringing the hip joint back into place"
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the pressure bandage, with which one wraps the books; and at two turns around the two heads of the two ribs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horn should be more delicate than the restrainer, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood should be two fingers wide, and its edge one finger thick, and one and a half palms long. And between the two joints there should be two attachments of this same wood, which are fastened at both ends with half a palm's length or a little more; and these two attachments are placed in the mouth of the wound to open it when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more delicate and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling tongs; and have two sockets at both ends, each a palm's length and two fingers wide. When you wish to open the mouth with the entire instrument, cause the woman to sit on the bed, her feet dangling and legs spread apart. Then insert both sockets together into the mouth, holding the head of the instrument beneath her thighs. Open your hand around the entire instrument, as you would with tongs evenly, according to how much you wish to open the mouth of the speculum.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	"These instruments are all mounted and have multiple similar forms. And when the master has prepared them, he who operates is faster in his work, and higher in esteem among men for his skill."
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	"Therefore do not disregard the instrument until you have prepared it, for its usefulness is not negligible."
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second child is retained during labor, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold her breath and then cause her to sneeze using condis. Hold your hands over her mouth and nose; if she expels something, all is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this is not the case, then take a pot, and make a hole in its lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as calamint, rue, anise, camomille, cassialigne, and centory; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in the pot with water over the fire. Then put one end of a tube into the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the marrow, and hold it until the vapors enter the marrow. Then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	"If the midwife acts quickly,"
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and is not yet healed, command the woman to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in musk of almonds, and then put it into nature, and seek the ovary. And when she has found it, grasp it gently and stretch it out little by little, straightly, so that the marrow does not fall out during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pull; thus it will come forth and be freed.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is too narrow, we have spoken of the cure for sneezing and fumigation with herbs; but if it does not improve from all that we have said, then be sure that you do not use the catheter; but what should be done at the mouth of the womb is to tie it to the woman's hip, then perform a suppository with terapharmacon ointment. She will recover and resume her activities, but even so, when she recovers there may still come forth an unpleasant odor in the stomach and head, which causes discomfort to the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	"Therefore, appropriate fumigations should be applied at this time. Many of the ancients have tried fumigations with watercress and dried figs."
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The shape of the instrument used for fumigation of the woman during childbirth and delivery is as follows:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles in appearance a dog's head. The subtlest part of its nature is placed on the fire, and the broad heads are laid upon the coals; let the fumigation be performed over the hot charcoal, until the resin is completely exhausted, then begin another.
de percier lou fondement	"to pierce the anus"
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born with the fundament not pierced, but blocked by a subtle sybac. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this sybac with her thumb and not to touch it with the sharp point of a spatula, guarding that she does not hurt it. Then place on wet linen soaked in wine and oil, then apply ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	"And if you suspect that it has not healed, insert a silver tube into the hole and leave it there for several days. It should be removed when the child is ready to go to its room."
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	"Sometimes this obstruction can be caused by a sudden eruption or boil. In such cases, the eruption should be opened and treated as described for the silver tube."
de la fistule dou fondement	"of a fistula of the anus"
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that originate beneath the anus are nodose, and growths that come around the anus or in the space of both buttocks indicate one fistula or several; and when this nodosity is ancient, it opens, and abundant white or clear mucus flows out, sometimes persistently; these fistulas are recognized by those who experience evacuation or wind during defecation by the patient, and occasionally one appears suddenly.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	"And there are fistulas that penetrate all the way to the bladder and halfway up the penis. Some reach as far as the hip joint, and others reach as far as the thighbone."
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes a persistent fistula at the anus, not a non-persistent one; and it is that you place your two index fingers on the anus, and insert a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, then insert a thin reed of brass or horsehair until you feel the reed or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, nor does any evacuation or wind or worm come from the opening, as we have said: know that it does not go through; so hasten to heal.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	"And when a fistula extends all the way to the bladder or the urethra, urine flows out of it and cannot be stopped with medications."
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the hip joint, then the coming tent is up to that place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around it, then it is that it has gone already astray, and neither medicine nor sudden ointment is worth anything in these Persian fistulas; and in these, there is no cure but labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is not Persian and not ancient, there is hope for healing with iron, as I have experienced, and it is necessary that the patient lies on their back in your hands; lift their legs up to their thighs, incline their thighs towards their belly; then insert a tent of brass, or lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must insert your two index fingers there, if now you sense that the tent has pierced it; and if uncovered where you sense between your thumb the sciatic nerve or the flesh, then know that it is Persian; so do not labor on it unless you can heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	All the time it is said that one can heal certain ones, but this happens little; and the aid that is made there, so it is that one heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before; and puts it all hot into the fistula until it reaches the fundament; and do this twice or three times, until you know that these broken-down tissues are burned, which resemble a feather; and then the cure with soft bandages smeared in butter, until this tissue comes off, then the cure with ointment between skin and flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed thus, all the better.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this one cannot be healed otherwise; and if the bandage enters but does not reach the fundus that is at the fundament, and there is a thick covering of flesh or skin between your two fingers and the bandage, and you see the fistula as it comes out from under the heart cover; then cut off from the beginning of the fistula, and immediately put in the bandage beforehand, and afterwards use the cautery until it reaches the end of the bandage; and the bandage will be delivered and will fall away; then remove those broken-down tissues that resemble a feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	"If the skin becomes inflamed, and cracks between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or strong medicine."
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Because the fire cautery combines two things: namely, the burning of adjacent flesh and the drying out of blood and moisture. Then treat wet wounds with burdock or ground bramble until the place becomes empty; and scrape away burned flesh from the wound. Then dress the wound with sudden ointments on hard skin, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	"For when it is thus restored, it will be healed and not return again."
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	"And if the fistula comes right up from the fundament but is distant from the body, push your thumb into the fundament and feel with it."
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel tension in the wound, and between two surfaces there is skin or fascia or flesh where it is about to burst, then apply fire cautery as we have said, or cut down to the bottom. If you cannot do this, put dressings on it and treat it as before; but do not cut too deeply lest you cut the tissue that holds the fundament, and cause unwanted discharges there. Then treat it as we have said. Perhaps it will heal without further intervention, otherwise remove that covering with a tent or other suitable instrument. Then cleanse the damaged flesh in the wound as much as possible, then study how to restore the wound and keep the fistula away from the fundament; thus it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: when you insert the tube into the fistula and it is located on the side near the foundation under the skin, take a pierced tube at its head according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	"And thread two turns of thread onto it, then insert the tent all the way down to its tip into the fistula."
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it pierces into the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that hole, so that you place your thumb on the foundation; and pull the head of the thread, and bring together the two heads, and tie them together, leaving it for one or two days. And sometimes tighten it again until the threads cut through those tissues that are between them and fall off; then dress the wound until it is healed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	"If the fistula does not open on its own, then make an incision in any way that you can, if it is not too deep."
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"For one should not cut too deeply for the sake of making a hole and then dress it as we have described until it is healed."
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatula used for opening a fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting, but not sharp on the other side, so that it does not cut what should not be cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	"hemorrhoids"
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorroids come in two ways: those that are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, which often bleed, and there can be one or more. Those that are outside have little moisture, and contain a little yellow water or a little blood, with the color of skin. The cure for those who have them inside the fundament is to instruct the patient to strain themselves while walking in rooms until the fundament emits them, and then grasp them; then hurry up, and grab them with forceps, or hold them with your thumbnail, then cut them at their roots. And if the thumbnail cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamlet, and pull them out with two fingers, then cut them, and apply some warm powders instead of cauterizing; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure them with other remedies until they are clean. And if the fundament cannot emit them, then administer to the patient a biting and harsh enema to wash what is inside the fundament so that it can come out openly. When the patient strains themselves, and if the threads are outside the fundament, then the cure is easy; it is only necessary to grasp them with thumbnail or forceps, cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are clean, and avoid incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you stitch according to this manner: take one twisted thread, and place it in a needle, then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce through on the other side, and turn both ends of the thread beneath the needle, and let them be wide; and pull the thread tightly, then tie the knot, and remove the needle, and do so with all the others, leaving one to correct the excess blood. Then place a warm oiled cloth or cerate over the wound, and have the patient rest; and then leave it until it closes, and once they are closed, cure them with ointment and other treatment until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	"on the drying of fistulas in the fundament"
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	"Sometimes there is a drying up of fistulas in the intestines due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine no longer helps;"
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must scrape off the scurf from the point of a scalpel or your nail without letting it moisten. Then treat it until it is sound as it should be. And if it cannot be made sound, then recommence scraping more forcefully than before until it is entirely clean and scraped. Then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	fever
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are tiny creatures that crawl throughout the body; sometimes they are found frozen, and their bite feels like death due to trembling, spreading throughout the entire body, more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	To cure this, take a reed from an ostrich feather or a strongulture's feather, and place it on the trembling spot until the circle encompasses the entire tremor. Then twist your hand around the reed, encompassing the tremor entirely, and push it deep inside to extract the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	"And if you see this, do so with a cane of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be thin underneath and pointed above:"
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	"However, do not pierce too deeply to hold the two together and apply pressure. And if you see this, cauterize the trembling, as it is said in front or in the chapter on cautery."
de la forme dou clistere	"of the form of the enema"
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	"No one ever makes an enema of silver or copper, or melted brass or lead; and no one ever makes them of these small and large instruments, according to which they are ordered."
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	"Therefore, those that should be used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful are small."
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	"The form of the small and large enema is as follows, where the belly is tied according to this manner:"
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a blockage or the belly is tied up, as you can see, with holes pierced inside it; and on one side there are two holes, and on the other one; and the belly is where medicines are placed in an animal bladder or parchment skin, pierced all around with small holes, each hole having a space of one finger-width between them. Then insert strong threads made from twisted hair into these holes, crossing them like an 'X' or winding them around, and assemble the belly like a goat's stomach. And when the medicine is inside, tie it closed with a strong string using the instrument beforehand, then administer the enema; this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicament not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or dove's fat, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister presses it with both hands together until it is completely inserted, then extract the clyster, and the patient lifts their legs to the bed, and if the medicament wishes to exit, so stretch it as much as one can; and if they lie awake all night, so there is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if you perform an enema on someone with diarrhea and the medication comes out quickly, then start it again until it is finished."
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, so let the clyster be as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of the subtle clyster upon which the skin should be restrained:
des plaies	"wounds."
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	"We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medications, according to their completion."
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	"I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to where the wounds are made, and what they are made from."
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by cutting with stone or sword and knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck or head or thigh or belly or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it's from an impact of stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt the formation of a hot boil: then make a poultice on the cephalic side immediately if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the poultice be contrary to the wounded part; and empty the patient's excess of wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want poultice, then thin out his diet, and let him drink no wine, nor eat flesh; and put on the wound, if a hot boil comes there, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in strictive wine. And if there is no hot boil, then put powder on the wound, all its blood fresh, and it is not moved by the air, which I will say later; and if the ars has moved it, then put on some ointments until it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	"And if the wound is large, like a cut from a sword or similar objects, and the lips cannot be brought together by force, then bring them together by stitching, as I will tell you about in the treatment of abdominal wounds."
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open and gaping and barely adhering to the bone, cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods like testicles and cooked wheat, also poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten skin and it is not on the bone, cut out all the rot, apply fire, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stanched by medicines without cutting, seek out the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	"And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: you should put in this powder that welds before the air has moved it."
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, grind it finely, apply the powder to the wound, bind it firmly until it draws well and joins with all its blood; then tie it well and leave it without removing it until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	"Sometimes this can also be done with quicklime alone when incense and dragon's blood are not available, but only if the air has not moved the wound."
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, especially in summer, do not apply this powder but instead use some digested ointments or poultices made from barley flour and honey mixed with water until it yields; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if bone fragments come with the wound and it is small, extract them using fine forceps; I will tell you about head fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	"Of the wound on the neck"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, except when the nerve of the neck or an artery is cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave it alone and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retreat; do not apply anything cold to the wound, as nerve substance is cold, and its continuation is with the brain which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water mixed with rose oil, and boiled cucumbers in soft water, and other warm stones ground in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the wound is large, then stitch it up with thread and bind it with bandages until it heals."
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the blood has gathered and filled it, then pierce it lower; and if an artery is cut, and blood flows freely, then drain it, bind it, cauterize it if necessary. And if the spine of the neck or the heart is wounded, keep in mind where the food goes, then lift the heart off the windpipe, not touching the throat but resetting it according to its natural shape; and then constrain carefully, leave for some days, then cure with drying ointments until it is healed. And if the wound has impressed upon the bone, cleanse it. And if there are bone fragments, remove them all if you can, those that cannot be had, let them stay until the wound putrefies and become drained and dressed; and if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	"And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, cure it as I have said in its chapter."
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	"Regarding wounds from spears or daggers,"
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a wound from a lance or dagger, and the wound is deep, observe if wind comes out of the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal. But if it is not deep, and all its blood is fresh, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor tie it up so that no air enters deeply and reaches the heart, causing death to the patient; but apply attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and let the patient lie on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor constraint of breathing. And when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then treat it with dressings and other treatments until it is healed. And if it cannot heal nor close up, then know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, then treat what is before you; if it's large, stitch it; if it's small, use powder. And if it's close to the bone and has cut pieces, clean the wound and dress it with hot compresses if they are severed; and if they aren't severed, let the wound fester until it softens for extraction; and judge other wounds on other limbs as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"Regarding rupture of the abdomen"
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And the ruptures of the belly are large and medium and small. Sometimes in a large wound, some intestine or part of it sticks out, making entry difficult; stitching is more painful, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because you can push the intestines back more easily with your fingers if you don't stitch them carefully. Also know that there are four ways to close a belly wound: two common stitches are used for closing the belly wound, and two other stitches specific to other wounds of the body are also used. However, those used for the belly wound are more appropriate, each of which I will describe.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines has been pierced, it is difficult to reposition, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen with cold.
