Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in this manner: soak a sponge or one clean cloth in hot water only, or cook in boiling water cinnamon and cumin and spikenard, and warm the intestines until the swelling has gone away; and sometimes do this with astringent wine, and also use a plaster to help reduce inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling diminishing, then moisten the intestines with water in which celery and mallows have been cooked, for by this means the entrance is enlarged a little; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision into the wound using the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is that one must not cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: so cut within the curvature and do not go beyond, as shown here:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude outwards, then put them back according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is located below the belly, then have the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head. And if it is located below the belly, then raise the head and breast higher than the lower parts. Similarly, if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, make sure that the wounded part is raised higher than the other. And thus you should arrange this for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you are equipped with. Then have between your hands one skilled assistant who will take all the rupture in their hand, and bring together the lips. And this is the common way of suturing: take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound. Then leave two inches from the head of the wound, and insert a needle with a strong thread. Pierce both layers of skin with both layers of sinew beneath it until you pierce them completely, then bring together all four edges together. Then tie a double thread around the needle on both sides, then bring together both edges of the wound neatly, and leave two inches, and insert another needle. Then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and continue this process according to what is needed with needles until the whole wound is closed. And the needles should be medium-sized, between fine and coarse, for too fine they cut all the flesh, and too thick will not penetrate well: therefore they must be medium-sized. Do not insert the needles too deep into the flesh and skin lest they tear open the wound before it is healed. Then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put tents or bandages over the needle holes to keep them in place until the wound is healed. This method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for one needle or two may suffice. The second way of suturing is common: bring together both layers of skin and both layers of sinew together with a needle that has a medium-strong thread. When you have pierced all these edges together, then draw the needle back to where you began, in the manner that cloth is sewn. And put between each stitch the thickness of a finger's width. This stitching is suitable for men, and I once sewed up a wound on a man's belly which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and his intestines were protruding out two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I reset the intestines for him after he had been feverish for 24 hours, and the wound healed up to the 15th day, which I cleaned, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle; and I did not dress the wound with any ointment, because there were none available where I was, nor any medicines; and I only put old cotton on the wound twice a day, washing it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: Take the needle and insert it from the outer part towards the inner until it pierces through to the other side. When it has pierced straight through the heart, then place the thread on top where you inserted the needle and make it pierce through from the inner part outwards; and the purpose of this stitch is that you sew like the furrier sews furs, leaving one side once before taking up the thread again so that the entire suture is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which Galen describes specifically, is thus: Some assemble the two parts naturally together and apply one end of the silk thread to the other in this way: Insert a needle near the edge of the wound and pierce only that spot, leaving both ends of the silk thread; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside until it reaches the inside at both ends of the silk thread; then pierce both again from the outside until it reaches the inside through two other needles placed on the opposite side. This is the proper manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word and some confirm it: One should stitch the abdomen with two needles, each having thread; one needle should be placed on one side and the other on the opposite, in the manner of those who sew hides. Know that when the wound is within the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other places on the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is as follows: When you find the wound fresh with all its blood before it has moved, first replace the intestines and the skin. Then apply powdered incense mixed with wax, and if it has moved, apply any available ointment until the wound closes. Then stitch the wound and bind it firmly with linen cloth and bandage; then treat the wound like others until it is healed. If you have no medicines, as soon as it begins to swell, apply old cotton immediately and stir it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But in many dispositions where wounds are simple, you have no need for other medicines. And if you suspect that the wound is communicating with principal limbs, then it is necessary to moisten lightweight linen in warm olive oil or rose oil and place it around the angles and under the armpits. And if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then perform black wine enema tinctures, especially if putrefaction reaches the intestines; pierce within and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines called "jejunum" cannot heal when wounded due to the thinness of their vessels and the delicacy of the entire body, as well as its similarity in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, replace it immediately like the intestines when fresh; but if it is old and has turned green or black, you must tie off the dark-colored part to prevent bleeding, as there are vessels and arteries present. Then cut away what is between the ties, and hang both heads down from below the wound until the spleen falls out, so that the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	from dislocation of the eyeball
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in certain people. I saw a man pierced in the belly with a lance; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, became inflamed, and turned into a fistula from which digestion and wind escaped. I applied treatment as best I could, and did not cease until he was healed, and his place was sound again.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him bound, I doubted that the patient had illness in his belly; but there was no illness, and he remained in better disposition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that if there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied in this manner: take pins with large heads, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it strains open its mouth, and then cut off its head, so that it cannot be untied; then place another pin afterward in the same manner as before until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These heads [of pins] often enter the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that is most skinless, and then tie at its head a thin twisted linen thread, then put the thread into the needle, and stitch up the intestine, and draw it through the opening; and this manner of pin stitching is no more than according to the way of trust and hope; but if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is neither remedy nor health except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	"of fistula wherever it may be"
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know this: any wound or abscess that becomes hollow is universally called a 'fistula,' and likewise when it swells and contracts.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is truly a hollowed-out wound with thick and white flesh, without pain, also swollen like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it clears up smoothly, other times thickly; sometimes small, other times large. I have already spoken about this in my division on wounds: any wound that does not heal because there is no flesh forming is due to one of eight causes: either the blood or flesh is too thin; or its nature is evil; or there is hard scar tissue inside and on the lips preventing flesh from forming; or there is too much swelling; or the area is putrid, with poor quality matter; or the medicine used was not good; or the corruption is of a pestilent nature; or digestion in that region is slow by nature, tardy in healing, and naturally inflamed. I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medicinal remedies in my division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	"Now I must tell you about the treatment of fistula which is done by manual work."
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries, and nerves, or to the bladder, or to the intestines, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so there are those that come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing else but work and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I have mentioned, and you trust in its cure, and recognize it, then take a tent of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, use it to search for it; and if the fistula is crooked, search for it with a subtle tent of lead, for lead bends more around the crookedness; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with tents, then rinse it with one of the openings, for moisture runs from one opening to another, and cleanses it. Then search for it by cutting according to what I have told you, and remove the fault and the corrupted flesh that are inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, then cut deeply as much as you can, then put moistened tents in hot medicine and place them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom. Then apply warm ointments made from healthy flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not bother the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it until all the corruption is gone, then treat things in a way that makes it healthy; and if it is not healthy, and swells back like before, know that you have not reached the bottom: uncover further and seek until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, so you cannot reach it; if there is no other way but to leave it to nature. But if there are some rotten small bones, and you can grasp them with forceps, then remove them with the appropriate instrument for this purpose. And if there are many bones, then remove them all, leaving none behind. And if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut away moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	Now if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something irritating to rot on the wound and let it sit until the surrounding area is entirely rotted. Then the bones will be easier to extract; but if it's a large bone such as that of the leg or thigh, simply scrape away the corruption until all darkness is gone, then restore the wound. And if there is a great portion of corruption reaching the marrow of the bone, you must cut everything up to the corruption and then treat it until solidified.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	A young man of about thirty years had pain in his leg due to an inner cause that made matter accumulate in the limb. A large abscess formed but there was no apparent reason for opening it. However, foolish physicians insisted on cutting into it repeatedly until a fistula developed with many holes through which bowels and moisture flowed from within the body. Many doctors tried to treat it over two years, but none were skilled enough to cure it. I was called in, examined his leg and his treatments, and saw that foul matter flowed out of the wounds making his skin red and yellowish.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then sought all the holes, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotted and perforated, and the corruption reached the bone inside; I scraped away what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought there was no other corruption besides that which I removed; and began to heal the wound with healing medicines for a long time, but could not close it; and then started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and scraped it away, and then removed it, and concerned myself with closing the place; but I could not do so until I cut around about a palm's breadth of the bone, and drew it out entirely to its root, then restored it with medicines; and it was healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because often blood was evacuated, but he became entirely healthy, and in place of the bone, hard flesh grew, and it was of good condition and had no harm or opposite at all, neither in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take linen, and tie it at the head of the exposed bone, and have someone pull upwards; then take another piece of thicker linen and bind it over the flesh above the bone, pulling the head so that you can draw out the rotting flesh below, and uncover the flesh on the spot where you wish to see, that the bone does not touch the flesh; and put a brand or hot stone under the bone to move the corrupt flesh away; this should be done as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and then repeated again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is decayed and does not appear, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, uncover all the flesh. Then place a hot iron underneath, and then sew from one side to the other the decay, and let the stitch be as long as the decay; thus we have said. And if the decay is at the joint, cut off the decayed joint and stitch the bone that contains it on the other side. And if the decay is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other option than to cut. And if the decay is in the wrist of the hand or in the ankle of the foot, that thing is very difficult, but nonetheless you must inquire how this decay opens. Cleanse it in all ways you can, but let not the vein nor the nerve hinder you. Know that there are many kinds of instruments to cut these bones according to their arrangement and appearance, their thickness and fineness, their size and smallness, their hardness. And for this reason, one must prepare an instrument suitable for each type of work. Know that the work will show you the instrument you need according to your knowledge of this art, and the evidence of the diseases' mannerisms. Thus consider the instrument you need accordingly.
dou feu	"from fire"
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head rots either due to internal causes or external causes. When you have treated this decay with medications but they do not help, then it is necessary to cut off that limb up to the point where the decay begins, so that the patient escapes death or the greater mischief of losing the limb. The sign is that the limb becomes black as if burnt by fire. Afterwards, this decay can spread from limb to limb and affect the whole body. Therefore, act quickly and if it is due to the sting of venomous creatures like sea scorpions, vipers, or similar ones, then cut off at the joint of the two fingers and do not allow it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cut off at the joint so that the decay does not reach the arm. And if it reaches the arm, cut off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, then death is imminent, and no remedies can save him due to the quantity of its power. And similarly, when decay comes upon the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut off after the next joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut off the whole foot; and if it goes up into the leg, cut off at the knee joint. And if it is above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to let the patient die. The method of cutting off or sewing up the limb is thus: you tie it above and below, extend some ministers one down from one tie and others upwards from the other tie, and cut open the flesh that lies between the two ties with a wide spatula until the bone is exposed; then cut off or sew up, and place on each side a linen cloth so that the wound does not touch the healthy area and cause further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs as you operate, quickly cauterize the wound with fire, or apply powders that restrain bleeding; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No boil ever comes in a narrow place that stays so long that it forms a large collection of pus; and then it bursts and spills out the pus, leaving the spot hollow like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a delicate veil, and does not penetrate to the bone or nerve, and such an illness is called 'sin' [sinus] and is not called 'fistula'; but if it is so long that it reaches down to the bone and goes deep, then it is called 'fistula'; and in this case you should cut away all of that skin entirely around it, even if it is delicate like a veil; and it does not matter for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin is hardened, and corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema thus: observe if the breast is large, and the bowel that enters it has a foul odor. Then use this Egyptian medicine made as follows: Take equal parts of aloe, oil, and litharge, and melt them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine becomes red-hot and as thick as honey. Then take some according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and administer the enema to the breast, plugging the opening tightly; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; repeat this many times until the breast is cleansed and the foulness removed. And sometimes use an enema of ash water when this medicine is not available; take ashes from burnt vine wood, pour water over them, let them cool, and administer as an enema until you know that the breast is well cleaned. If the patient cannot tolerate this, nor the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then use an enema of water and honey with a little powdered litharge added; or use an enema of honey and mixed wine that has properties to cleanse and wash, and makes the flesh harden. And when you have done this, and believe that the breast is well cleansed, then administer an enema of such things as cause new flesh to grow there; take diachylon plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine. Or use other medicines and ointments whose properties I have mentioned in the section on ointments. And if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter, then widen it slightly with an iron tool, and insert a wick of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened sufficiently; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up and leave only the place where the enema can enter. And if the opening that admits the bowel is above, then cut lower down so that it enters.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bowel is deeply prolapsed, do not allow any flesh to enter; and if you cannot grasp the lower part of the breast as you wish, then arrange it in such a way that the bowel goes to its lowest position, for when the bowel is deep, no flesh should enter it. And if you cannot grasp the lower part of the breast as you wish, then arrange it in this manner: let the bowel run easily downward, and leave nothing of the bowel; and take consolidative medicines to put on the skin, and stretch over all the skin with a linen cloth; then cut strongly towards the opening of the breast somewhat larger than the first, for afterwards every day once remove the large outer cloth; and that which is on the opening of the breast, often remove it to remove the bowel, and know what comes from the bowel, whether it's venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been thus extended and you see the nature that rises on the opening of the breast, then know that the breast is already healed, and approaches health. And then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if after many days the breast continues to secrete undigested milk, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair of health, for recovery is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If it happens that wounds take a long time to heal or conversely heal too quickly, and if undigested food rises from the stomach after many days without causing pain in the stomach, know that the stomach is not injured; but if the stomach takes a long time to digest, and is far away, apply drying medicines in substance and power, such as diachylon ointment, for it contains much vitriol, which is the last medicine. Prepare diachylon ointment with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine; then cook it and use it accordingly. And likewise, when diachylon ointment is not present, take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, grind them into powder, and sprinkle on honey while it is over the fire. Then place the cloth on the stomach and apply it. Sometimes also administer long aristologia root and celestine roots, which are also like barley flour and centaury; use simples or compounds: grind them and make a powder, and sprinkle on the honey mentioned earlier, and use accordingly. And if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, know that the corruption has gone deep and has made an impression on the bone or hard member or ligaments. Then the treatment for fistulas should be applied, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil of the toe
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that originates beneath the nail of the thumb of the hand, or of the foot, or sometimes occurs in other toes; and when it becomes old and is not taken care of, so then comes a hard abscess, which runs and spreads until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it runs all over; and the corrosion reaches to the bone, so that there is foul-smelling pain, and the head of the toe becomes large, and the color becomes dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we have said in the section above and yet the treatment does not help, then you must cut away with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, after which cauterize the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is very helpful if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy. However, if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to hurt and blister, then you must insert a narrow blade beneath the nail that pricks the flesh and push it up, cutting away that delicate flesh gently and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines onto the remaining flesh to remove all of it. Then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and apply fire, for as long as the rotted bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see both rotting, cut into one of them as it was said before, then treat it until it heals; and if it is infected and inflamed, causing great pain, you must first cleanse it; then cut the edge of the shoulder blade in a diagonal cut across, ensuring that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of gout in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Some people are sometimes born with both hands completely fleshy, and sometimes there is bone in them, and sometimes there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in certain fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those born with extra fingers do not move them, and those born at the joint of the hand sometimes can move them; cut off the fleshy one in this manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure, so he should hold onto the cover
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born deaf or becomes deaf later on, you should first cut the flesh around the bone all the way to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and then polish it until it is smooth.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sinews that come together at the two joints come by birth, or by the union of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you must cut that scar so that the ears regain their natural shape. Afterwards, place between two wet cloths or bandages soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick together; or place between two thin pieces of lead until the place is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling occurs on either side with the palm, scrape away this scurf as needed.
des vils	(of villains)
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large folds filled with melancholic superfluities that come from various parts of the body. More so in legs of those who walk and work, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him a laxative for the colon, and then the holy water of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cautery of fire is done in two ways: one is by cutting and drawing out the black blood; the other way is to raise the vein and draw it out entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The surgeon proceeds in this manner: first, apply a hot water bath to the leg very strongly until the thick blood is thinned. Then press on the leg of the patient from above the hip down to just below the knee; next, cut the vein at point I, II or III with a wide blade, then squeeze and draw out dark blood by hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient's strength can bear; then bind it and instruct him to abstain from black cabbage; and resume evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, but this harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The way to raise the vein is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and apply hot water until the leg turns red and the veins swell. If you have no bath, heat it by the fire, then cut at the vein near the long part above the knee or below the ankle; then cover the skin with an onion, and scrape the vein on each side until it appears when touched, and it looks red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white rope; then put the hook underneath until it raises from the skin, then lift it with the onion gently, then cut in another place three fingers above; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the hook as you did before, then cut another incision if necessary, then lift and cut at the two ends of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second incision; then extract it incision by incision until it all comes out, then cauterize it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert a needle with strong double thread, tie and pull it, and put it under the hook and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out. Be careful that it does not cut, for if it cuts, one cannot pull nor lift it, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have completely treated it, place damp wool in vinegar and rose oil on the wound, and dress it until it is clean.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the sinew is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cut off all of it; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron tool used to cut the sinew is curved, and it does not cut straight, so that it does not cut into the vein; and it should be thickly curved, for if it were thin, it would cut into the vein, but let it be thick as we have said; here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in hot regions where there are no herbs or trees growing, and on dry land with no moisture; and sometimes it grows elsewhere besides the legs, which happens due to rot that comes beneath the skin, like how snakes and worms enter between the skin and flesh inside the body.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that there comes a very great inflammation in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to protrude outward like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, then you must wrap around it a piece of lead measuring one and a half to two fingers wide, and tie it; leave the lead hanging from the leg, and each time it starts to bleed, wrap the lead around it again and retie it. And if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the remainder, but do not cut it at its root, so that it does not reenter the flesh and cause an abscess or decay in the area, leading to a bad illness; for this reason, it must be treated bit by bit up to its end, leaving nothing on the body. And sometimes this vein is as long as five or ten palms when it has been treated, and once a man came to me whose was ten palms long. And when you cut it, place one arrow in the opening and pierce it all the way down so that everything comes out; empty the matter inside it, and bring healing remedies to apply against decay for several days, then dress it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is very large, especially when it opens at the ankle joint or on the foot, and many wounds appear from which much blood flows; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land 'cattle disease,' because it often happens to oxen. It is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, ascending and descending, moving from limb to limb until it reaches the skin where it breaks out, causing sores. This is due to corruption of certain humors, like worms, serpents, leeches, and ascarids in the belly. Doubt exists about its severity because when it travels through the body, if it reaches the head, it may enter the eye and destroy it; this happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one can only do so when it is moving. Therefore, tie the skin above and below with a strong, tight string, then cut and pull it out. If the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and cannot be found, cauterize the area with fire until it dies. The greatest harm it causes is when it runs towards the eye, as we have said. If you see it coming near the head close to the eye, press down firmly on the eyebrow below it, then cut and pull it out. The patient should use bodily cleansing with medicinal solutions for corrupt humors, and avoid eating foods that cause corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From pain caused by windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vaquería" in our land, and it is a pain that comes into certain limbs, and moves from limb to limb; I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a woman who was ill. She showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm. And shortly after, it climbed like a worm to the shoulder, as swift as quicksilver moving from one place to another; the pain left that spot, and stuck itself in the shoulder, then it soon spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm. She then told me that she was continually turning around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I was greatly amazed at how she moved from limb to limb in this way, for I had never seen this disease manifest itself like this before."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had heard many times that pain could move from one place to another, but I had never seen it happen like this in a woman. And I thought that this happened because the woman had a dry body and uncovered veins, which allowed this constraint windiness to appear; whereas it does not appear according to this reason in those who are dislocated, and have moist bodies and concealed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then place heat above and below hastily, and then cut until that constrained wind escapes from its place; and cauterize the place; and if you cannot see it with your eyes, then treat it with remedies that drive out winds, such as fetid pills and pills of saffron, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"The causes of hiccups are varied according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they occur."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The varieties of them are such that there are some which have large points and small ones, and barbed and welded; and those which have two angles, and those which have long shafts, and those where there are pieces broken off; and those that fall into any limb fall in two ways: either into principal limbs, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore into any place in these limbs, and the signs of death that I shall tell you hereafter appear to you: then it is necessary that you beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes afterward in many ways; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out and dress the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the skull when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and jumps the sinew that is upon the skull, is when there is darkness and dizziness and faintness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes it goes without fever from the nostrils or ears; and sometimes it loses speech and voice; and blood comes out of the wound white like feathers, and also burns of flesh; and if these signs appear, then you should attend to the cure, and remove the arrow if it is not already embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	And the sign of the arrow when it falls upon the heart is that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were struck into something hard, not empty; and sometimes the arrow moves like a feather, and black blood comes out in a clot, and coldness and cold sweat come on, and fainting: then you shall know without doubt that the person is dying.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"The sign of hiccups that occur near the lung is when foamless sputum suddenly comes from the wound; the throat swells up and the patient changes color, sighs loudly, and seeks cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	"And if hiccups occur in the covering of the stomach, near the ribs, they cause much belching and great pain with sighing; all the members of the shoulders move."
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if hiccups occur in the stomach, sometimes undigested meat comes out from the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if hiccups occur in the belly and blood flows through the intestines suddenly, there is no hope of recovery or extraction of the hiccup."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	"And if hiccups occur in the bladder and urine suddenly comes out with blood, and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is mortal."
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"Other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary muscles, spinal column, buttocks, thighs, and legs, etc., are safe according to many conditions."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When hiccups occur in a nerve or artery and are not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do the same."
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one that an arrow struck him near the root of his nose; I probed it and drew it out from beneath the ear's fat without causing harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And drawn out was an arrow that struck the fat of the eye beneath its membrane, and the arrow's head had entered, but only its point could be reached towards the timber, and it was large like a Turkish bow, all of light iron without ears; the patient was healed, and no ill accident befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And an arrow was drawn from the throat of a Christian, and it was Arabian with ears; I cut its barbs and carefully drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And an arrow was drawn from one who had fallen in the belly and thought he would die; but after thirty days his condition did not change; I cut into the arrow, crafted a hook, and drew it out without causing harm.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man struck by an arrow on the back, and the wound has healed over it; and the arrow remains inside him, and did not change its natural position, nor cause harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another man struck by an arrow in his face, and the wound has healed over it; and remained thus without causing great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow was drawn from the prince's eye of the king, which had fallen into it and was slightly inclined towards the right side; and the arrow was completely buried when I was called for treatment three days after it fell.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	Using all my skill and care, I could not feel it; but he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I put on the affected area an attractive, digestive plaster to prevent inflammation; and the head of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for many days and reopened the wound, and thus the patient remained for a long time until he felt the arrow in his flesh one day later.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed a corrosive medicine on the wound for many days until it opened, and tested it; I felt the head of the arrow sticking in its place. Then I inserted this medicine into the opening of the wound so that the head of the arrow became visible; this lasted about four months. After this, the wound healed over so much that I could not remove the arrowhead with forceps.
