Therefore, I did not cease to devise ways and means using various instruments until, one day, I took hold of it with well-made forceps, according to what is described at the end of this chapter; thus I drew it out and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I then set it right, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient became entirely sound.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you about the qualities of extracting certain arrows; therefore, do not rely on what I have not mentioned, for books cannot cover everything. However, wise masters examine even small details and find new works and tools based on present and missing information in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows come out of the limbs where they are stuck in one of two ways: either through the point where they entered or through another part. Those that come out through the place where they entered are called 'entering' arrows, and sometimes this happens suddenly.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out suddenly, leave it alone until the flesh rots around it and the exit is opened. Similarly, if it is stuck in bone and cannot come out on its own, leave it alone for a few days and move it gently each day. Then it will come out; but if it still won't come out, carefully cut around it with a fine knife until the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bone of the skull and goes into one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the symptoms I mentioned appear in the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it there for a few days until it becomes even, because if the arrowhead comes into the brain, death will result.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrowhead is stuck only in the bone and does not reach the brain, and the patient remains for some days without bad symptoms, then you can attempt to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is very deeply stuck and cannot come out, then apply poultices around it as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrowhead is buried in the flesh so that one cannot see it, then search for it carefully. And if you feel it, pull it out with some appropriate instrument. And if you cannot do so because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins there, then widen the wound until it is large enough. Then pull out the arrowhead if you can. And if there are barbs on the arrowhead by which it holds fast, cut away the flesh that is stuck in both sides of the wound as much as you can. Then break or bend the barbs of the arrowhead so that you can pull it out without breaking it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot do it all at once, leave the arrowhead until the wound around it is healed, then pull it out, for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if blood flow opposes you, then follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter; and beware of the nerve incision and the vein, and consider how you can carefully pull out the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position they were in when the arrow struck them, for that is the greatest help. And if you cannot do so, then place them according to what signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow came from another side, where something of it can be seen or the skin is swollen there: cut until you can grasp it with forceps, and then extract it.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, twist your hand round until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be extracted, leave it for now and then restart the extraction until it comes out. And if the shaft of the arrow is there, remove the entire shaft. And if the shaft has fallen and you see that pushing is necessary, use the hooked instrument so that the tip of the arrow enters the hook of the instrument; then push it out, and if the arrowhead is hooked, insert the instrument with its pointed end to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead has touched the lung,
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls into the foot or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close, you can probe for it; guard against probing the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then suture the wound if necessary; care until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat splints is similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like that of a bird's feather, for striking at the tip of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pliers for attaching and removing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common flesh
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The thirty-one veins from which one bleeds are as follows: sixteen at the head, namely: two temporal arteries behind the ears called 'dou Herbech'; and two arteries appearing in the temples; and two veins in the corners of the eyes called 'aspirers'; and one vein in the forehead; and one vein at the back of the nose; and two jugular veins in the neck; and two veins above the mouth, which are called 'augeherich'.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used in each arm are three: one is the cephalic, and it lies along the left side, and laypeople call it "the vein of the head"; and the median is called "deep," and it consists of the cephalic and basilica, and laypeople call it "the vein of the heart"; and the basilica lies along the right side, and laypeople call it "the vein of the belly," and it is above the fibula, and this is the one that opens up clearly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the "savate" vein is between the little finger and ring finger, having two branches; and in the leg there are three veins: one under the bend of the left pouch, and the second saphenous vein on the right ankle; and the vein called "nese," which is at the other ankle's heel; and there are three more veins under those in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins behind the ears help in ancient treatments and bleeding. The quality of the bleed is as follows: raise the patient's head and rub where the veins are with a rough cloth. Then have the patient tighten their neck with a bandage until two veins appear behind the ears, hanging from the top. Then feel for the pulse beneath your fingers, and press gently. Take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone. Then lift your hand upstream along the vein and cut both layers of skin and vein deeply enough that blood flows freely. Then press and bind until it stops bleeding.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Bleeding from the two arteries in the temples is useful for ancient treatments and for sudden illnesses, and for customary eye treatments, and for wet eye pain. The method of bleeding is as follows: Have the patient tighten their neck until both veins appear clearly. Then feel the pulse beneath your fingers and press gently. Next, raise your hand to place your index finger on top of the vein and insert the lancet underneath, lifting the vein upward and cutting it as you did with the other two veins, allowing blood to flow according to necessity. Then release the patient and hold your finger over the vein for an hour before applying cotton. Finally, bind it tightly until it stops bleeding. We have already spoken about their cutting and extraction in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting from the frontal vein is as beneficial as that from the cephalic for treating old facial diseases, and for migraines, and redness. The characteristic is that the patient strains their neck in twisting, so much that the vein appears; then they take the tool called "fosseur," of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point upon the vein and press with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow according to what you see fit; then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it stops bleeding and sometimes use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not necessary for the bandages to be too tight; and tie them diagonally, because the bone is nearby, and by chance the bandage may break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting from the two veins that are in the temples is beneficial for the eyes and for dizziness and redness of the face, and for inflammation of the eyelids. The characteristic of their bleeding is that the patient strains their neck while turning one way or another, as previously described; then let the blood flow across, a bit long and wide, since there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandage is too thin, it may break. Then let out blood according to your necessity and then tie on cotton, tying it tightly
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	For the cauterization with fire, instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; if they are prickly at their base, hold their eyes steady so that they do not move until they grow.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	For the cauterization of the two veins [in the elbow], it helps with strangury, and the beginning of catarrh, and many illnesses, and measles, and corrosives, and herpes, and nosebleeds. The procedure is as follows: the patient should tilt their head to one side and another, as we have said; then let the master be standing on the patient's head, and the patient sitting on a chair. Then cauterize the vein for a short time somewhat widely, and draw blood temperately or as much as necessary. Then do the same in the other vein, untie the ligature, and press gently around both veins so that the patient does not strangle; leave it until the morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sanctity of the veins above the lips helps with coughing in the mouth and with gum corrosion, lip fissures, nosebleeds, and around the nostrils
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of health are such that you should have the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I've said; then turn their lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which are known by being black, and by having small black veins around them: therefore cut both of them, and if you do not know them or are in doubt, cut the largest from each side, and do likewise for the two veins that are above and below, as this is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of the veins that are beneath the tongue aids after the cephalic bleed, and is used for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and its qualities are such that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, raises their tongue, and looks beneath each side for a black vein: therefore cut one and the other, but do not go too deep, as beneath them lie the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm are commonly opened in two ways: either by pricking with a broad-pointed instrument like a lancet, or with an olive-shaped, pointed one like a knife tip, and these are called "anesil"; they are broad and pointed according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the myrtle flame is very well-known, and it is wide as you see
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary for opening hairy veins full of visible thick blood, and containing thick and turbid blood; and this is the shape of the olive-pointed lancet.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed and is for healing thin veins that contain clear yellow blood
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps those with illnesses under the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen. And the veiner must vein skillfully and beware of the artery that lies beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he hits the artery and blood starts flowing, then it must be stanched as I have said; and the point of the lancet should not be prickling but cutting like an 'anesil'.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilisk does not open up clearly, then you must extract it and replace it with another; or if you wish to perform some operation on it, or sew in its place the vein within the arm: it opens up clearly; and cauterize the wound with fire.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to recognize the location of the vein, then first extract the arm, touch the location until you feel the pulse; then mark the location with ink, and tie the arm, cauterize the vein with fire. And be careful not to strike the artery when you see the location swell, for it is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see something swell up high like urine from a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: hurry quickly then, place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; tie the arm, leave it thus, and do not let the patient move it; be careful, do not let him move until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and you faint, and there is no physician present, then cut the artery if it is open for the sake of the head; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig tree bark, and cut it, then take one half and tie it firmly until the next day; if blood oozes out, that's good. If not, treat it with powders that stop bleeding, as we have said; these stoppings are not harmful in many situations due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's ligature.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bandage of the vein in midsection helps draw blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said. The surgeon must be careful about the nerve underneath, and if he pricks too deeply, and hits the nerve, inflaming it, then the wound may not heal; this nerve opens frequently, but in some men it does not open due to its fineness, so you must use an instrument called the anserine vein finder. Avoid damaging the nerve with all your strength.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is space between the two nerves, make an incision along it
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bloodletting of the cephalic vein helps by drawing blood from the head and aids in eye disorders; and it is preferable to perform bloodletting at the elbow olive or the elbow mirtin, for this is the safest of all veins as there are no nerves nor arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one should seek the easiest location, and if it fails at first, try again without causing any harm. Sometimes the area may swell in some people when it is attempted for the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the surgery depends on your skill.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is only performed to preserve health and prevent future illnesses. It should be done in one of the three veins located on the arm: the cephalic, basilic, or median basilica vein. Bloodletting should begin during Lent at the start of winter and autumn, after meals when signs ofpletion appear. It should be done on either the first or third day of the week, two or three hours after noon.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The balm that is administered to the sick has no fixed time, but it must be given when needed by day or night at all hours and at all times; and one should not anoint children up to 14 years of age nor women during the four months after giving birth until seven days have passed.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one operate on the elderly who have passed sixty years of age
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be anointed, in whatever manner it may be, they must first cleanse the intestines with a light enema if there is much retained feces so that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the intestines into the principal members; nor should one anoint someone who is too salty from eating meat or who is drunk until he is sober again, nor those who are dropsical. And one should not anoint after a bout of colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive menstruation in women, work, wakefulness, fasting, or anything that uses up all strength; then refine the humors with foods and drinks and medicines if you have the power to do so; then enter into a bath if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood, and anoint from the vein on the arm around the third part as we have said; and guard against work, eating, lust, and similar things that day; be cheerful and joyful, and let the anointing person stand higher than the one being anointed, and rub his arms twice or three times, then stretch the lien over the middle, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow properly; then wet the finger of his left hand with a little old oil and place it on that vein below where he wants to anoint, so that the vein does not swell or burst from the striking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flee like cords to the sinew, and some such are full of windiness so that when one puts on the flame it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus many are injured; and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first try, that is good; but if not, then restart a little lower or higher, as long as the area is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen and the patient fears it, let him rest for one or two days without tying up his arm: perhaps white abscesses will come forth; do not go into a bath afterwards, then recommence the cautery if he pleases; and if the hole is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it does not flow enough, then apply all the flame directly to that hole; and burn it a little hastily before the place becomes swollen; for often this happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not recommence the cut, and put upon it a bit of oil ointment, for it lightens the body's blood, and in this place the oil has power to soften what is hard; and thus administer the oil ointment in each cut that you make into veins, to stop the flow of blood; and it does the same thing for liver and lung, when put upon the place; so subtlely does the blood thin out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess appears there, which happens often, especially when it is not cut for any other time than that single opening of the vein, then hurry and put upon the place sponge moistened in water and heated over some heat for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has stopped flowing from the vein, and if it remains on the place for a few days with some blackness or greenness, do not worry about it; and if you see, put upon it something of aloe or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, masterwort, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is swelling and appearance of inflammation at the time of surgery like that of the basilisk: therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the area soft under the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to apply any of the remedies we have mentioned, for perhaps blood would flow from the artery; but instead make one dry dressing to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw off blood according to its quantity and according to its color.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if it is thick, let it flow until it becomes thinned; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and robust, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and the flame be wide; but for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is fitting to lance shallowly and often, and one should lance by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of letting blood saves from loss of blood and injury to nerves, and is better than a long or wide lance.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body fails at letting blood, give them a moistened powder made from pomegranate juice; if they are heated, let three or four bleedings be done. And if they are of cold complexion, before letting blood, let them eat bread moistened in thickened mucilage syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing much blood, afterwards he should inhale broth of flesh, and fragrant subtile syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the chapter on syncope for evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to empty the arm vein and be bled again later, it is necessary that when he is weakened by much bloodletting, he be bled little by little according to his continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to empty the arm vein after the first bloodletting and has a strong body, should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to have blood drawn from another vein should be bled on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood inside the body that is already heated and causes fever; so it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and widen the opening until it reaches the forearm; then when you have attended to all the conditions of fainting, place your hand on his pulse when he faints, so that the blood does not return to the forearm, which happens often when the attendant is careless; and this is not necessary if you see that you must loosen the arm and cause blood to flow out again, nor if the opening is curved should he quickly extend his arm, for that would be bad; but let him remain until he faints a second time; or you can cauterize with the tip of the flame until the frozen blood at the vein's opening flows out, then place some cotton soaked in water on it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not squeeze it until the inflammation has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a necessity to draw blood a second time, do so in the same vein or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are bled in place of the head vein because they are connected.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of cauterizing is thus: The patient immerses their hand in warm water until the blood vessels become red. Then tie it moderately so that the vein appears well. Now cauterize across, not wide or long. Make the opening large and cauterize close to the joint of the hand. If blood does not flow out, immerse the hand again in warm water and let enough blood flow into the water. If it is summer, do not immerse the hand again in warm water because more immersions are done in winter than in summer. The cauterization of this vein is safer than all others as there is neither artery nor nerve present.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cauterization of the saving vein of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases. Here's how: Press on the hand and immerse it in warm water until the vein swells so that you can see it. If you cauterize across and cut completely throughout, there will be no discomfort. However, do not go too deep because nerves lie beneath all skin surfaces. Then put the hand back into warm water if blood is congealed in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And once you have cleaned off as much blood as necessary, then place a bandage of oil and flax to quickly bind the wound, and do this for each wound."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The swelling in the left hand is attributed to mouse disease, so perform the same treatment as I have instructed for the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the spleen is beneficial for all ailments beneath the body, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of fluids, diseases of the reins, and old afflictions of the thighs and legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are that the patient places his foot in hot water, and rubs it on the vein until it breaks, and then binds the ankle joint; this vein is at the ankle, and many kidneys go up along the leg; therefore, heal where the largest kidney or at the ankle, which moves better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	"And if you cauterize on the foot, beware of the nerves beneath it, and make the cautery like a cut; and let the flame be gentle."
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if the blood cannot flow out, then put the foot back in the water and allow the vein to drain well."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the salve fails the first time, then apply it again a little higher up, for the spot is salty; do not fear nerve damage, as we have said, and do likewise with the spleen salve of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle joint, and its cauterization benefits sciatica pain when it is due to hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its salve are that the patient enters into a bath and presses above the ankle with four fingers while twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then apply the salve in all ways you can, including transversely; and it is better that you cover it, for the spot is dry and it becomes very swollen on many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then choose any vein that opens at the foot's heel, towards the little toe, and beware of nerves. And make sure to bind the blood vessel tightly until you see blood, then untie it, and place cotton on top and secure it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	And regarding cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	"Cupping vessels are made of horn, or earthenware, or glass; and cupping is performed in two ways: either by pricking to attract blood, or without pricking."
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping treatment that does not involve bloodletting is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire. And the cupping treatments that are performed by pricking and drawing blood are carried out on fourteen parts of the body: one is entirely on top of the head, another is in the neck, two others are on both sides of the neck, one below the chin, two on the shoulders, two on the hips, two on the arms, two on the legs, and two on the ankles. Cupping treatments do not draw blood, except for a few scattered veins in the flesh, so they do not weaken at all like those done by vein cautery. They should therefore not be administered with or without fire in any disease caused by repletion until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to illness to relieve oneself, or due to customs, then administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and also in between and at all times; for there are those who, when they need to relieve themselves, have a heavy head; and there are those who findpletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and such as find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have an enlarged tongue, and faint; and there are those who dream, and see by nut blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	"And when we see these signs, especially if they occur during the month, we order cupping to be performed after three hours of the day."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The discharge of mucus helps with the dryness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be done after the evacuation of all bodily waste; and this discharge replaces the discharge of the cephalic, and those who are of cold complexion should not use it, or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm; and therefore old men should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful, so one must place the cupping vessel a little lower down to avoid forgetfulness."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Wind in the neck is located at the junction of the head and the spine. Therefore, it benefits from the stretching of the breast and the splitting of the vessels of the diaphragm, and from sudden movements and fullness; but one should put little pressure on it, for if it holds too firmly, it can cause dizziness in the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Wind in the second cervical vertebra causes headaches and eyestrain, migraine, and strangling pain at the roots of the teeth. It is located at the junction of the spine. You must instruct the patient to press their hand gently when applying the cupping glass, so that it does not cut the artery or cause excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	"Cupping under the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, gum inflammation, and similar conditions that are in the mouth; it is in lieu of bloodletting from both lips."
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"Cupping on the shoulders is beneficial for illnesses that come from heat and excess;"
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Wind in the ribs is beneficial for three veins of the arm because it draws blood from those large veins. Instruct the patient not to heat the cupping glass too deeply, as that area lacks flesh and contains nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	"A cupping vessel placed on the buttock is beneficial for hemorrhoids and lower abdomen diseases. The vessel should be large and made of brass to draw well; if it were too thin, it might break and cause large wounds."
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	"Cupping on the legs draws openly, for it attracts blood from the whole body and is beneficial for old back pains, sciatica, bladder inflammation, and it strengthens the flesh. It is in lieu of the two sophenes (groin muscles) and the two ankles, but it can also weaken the body with prolonged use and cause edema in various conditions."
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	"The method of applying the cupping vessel is as follows: first place it empty and suck gently but steadily. Then apply it quickly and move it evenly until you see the area turn red and swollen, and the skin becomes flushed. Then remove it and replace the vessels. Be cautious about the condition of the body, for some people have thin flesh and clear pores; in this case, one should strike only once and make wide but not too deep wounds. Suck gently."
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	"If the blood is thick, then one must strike twice: the first time to refine the path of the thick blood."
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	"And if the blood is very dense, one must strike a third time. But if we wish to draw only a little blood, once will suffice."
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we desire much blood, let us recommence often; and if the blood is thick, let us fire a dart deeply, and let the end be such that the heart is pierced suddenly; and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you apply the places of cups with aperitive and dissolvent oil: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, of cress oil, or of lily, or camomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	"And if the excess blood is thick and cold, use myrrh oil, balsam oil, fennel oil, or similar."
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one whose skin is tender and has wide pores is treated with a cautery, no oil should be applied there, but it should be washed afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	"And those with excessive moisture should rise using hyssop water, myrtle water, sumac water, or similar substances."
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive fullness rise from old wine or clear water, or decoction of fennel or chamomile, or others alike; and it is not necessary to use a cupping glass before or during the bath, but afterwards one hour or two after the bath; and do not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that he be cautious when he must undergo cupping and when he undergoes cupping.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware those who have undergone cupping are choleric, and their blood is too hot and inflamed; therefore they should consume cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce with vinegar, and similar things; and eat figs, and castrated meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have cold complexion should consume honey syrup, and moderately fragrant wine which is between old and new, and eat pears, and figs, small birds and chickens; and on the day that he undergoes cupping, he should drink more than he eats; and sometimes it is necessary to give some people treacle or muscat before or after cupping, to strengthen the main limbs; but let the blood be subtilized, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Ventouses applied without pricking are those placed on the liver, womb, podagra, belly, thigh, and back. These members do not tolerate being pricked and this is done only to draw blood from one member to another, as we apply them to the breasts when there is inflammation; to remove viscosity from the member, as we apply ventouses to the belly and thigh to slenderize it; and to alleviate pain where there is obstruction or stone, perhaps drawing off the obstruction through its attractive power, or displacing the stone from its place. Thus they act when placed on the liver and womb when there is retained windiness, these ventouses being administered empty merely to suck. Sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in pleurisy cases, so that one fills the ventouse with hot water only, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of administering the cupping glass with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on the side around the middle one small hole like for inserting a needle, made of brass or iron, smooth at its tip so it doesn't cut the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle have a transverse bar of brass or iron for placing an imprisoned candle, and let there be both large and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who use them; for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of elders, and those of the thin are different from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And you should place this cupping glass on the limb thus: take a candle of wax or flax and put it inside the cupping glass through the bar that is within it, so that its flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass lest it burn the patient; then place it on the limb, ensuring that the two holes we mentioned are on top, so that when you wish, steam can escape, and you remove the cupping glass; and take the flax as before, and repeat it often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping procedure used for pleurisy with acute inflammation, it has neither stalk nor hole and is not filled with fire unless when it is full of air, and is placed only on the limb; that is its shape.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without fire are used those cupping procedures that cannot be applied where cups are too small, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places without flesh, such as the toes or nose, and others like them. The quality of this procedure is that when you find leeches that are in sweet, clear waters without any damage, you take them; and put them one by one in sweet water until they become accustomed and have nothing inside their bellies; and then prepare the vein and the cupping procedure, rub the limb until it becomes red, and place the leeches on top. And when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where you can apply a cup, apply one, for this works greatly afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not so, then raise the level with oil first, and then with water very well, and then squeeze it. And if the level rises too high on the body of the veins, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on until the blood is stanched. And if the blood increases too much, then put powdered vitriol or salt, etc., until it is stanched; or you may put half a handful of peeled peas on the level, and leave them until they adhere to the level, now it will be stanched. And if you still need more, then take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins refuse to take, then rub the level with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the blood flows out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are falling off, then powder some alum and celandine leaves crushed together, or ashes, so they will stick now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and provides treatment for broken bones and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear son, that foolish physicians throw themselves into this chapter without ever having seen any of the old books or read a letter of them; and for this reason knowledge is estranged in our land, for I found none good; and know nothing save through the science of the old books whereof I have studied so much that I have treated the science therein, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have briefly described to you here what is contained in this chapter and abridged it at the end, clearly showing the forms of instruments that are arranged thus as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the sums of speech and chapters where the wise places his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are tried may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or bruising happens to anyone, then you must hasten to treat the patient on both sides if nothing prevents you from doing so, such as weakness of body, childhood, old age, or if time is not very hot nor too cold; and avoid eating cold things, namely cold drinks, and bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, nor fill yourself too full with foods that fill the veins with blood until you doubt the formation of a hot boil or expansion of matter in the limb. Let the patient return to his usual diet as he has used it before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the sick person with foods that promote growth and have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pears, and veal, eggs, fresh fish, and similar things, and strong wine."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this nourishment the wound will close more quickly and completely."
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the elderly and frail do not heal well nor set properly due to the weakness of their limbs, nor those that are too soft like the bones of young children; but without care, align the broken bone with large splints that hold the limb together until it heals as before; do not remove all the points of its work, and therefore it is necessary to feed them coarse meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that breaks are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For a break of the head is different from a break of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways that bones can break."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"For there are breaks that happen suddenly, and others that occur gradually, such as when cutting a feather to make a writing pen."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there is also breakage with wounding, and breaking with just a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own instrument and proper device in the restoration, according to how the limb comes into its place; and bone fracture is known by the twisted joint, clearly apparent by touch, and audible under pressure of the hand; but when there is no twisting nor sound upon touching, and the patient feels little pain, then there is no fracture; yet it may have some twisting or cracking or minor break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb by hand, but apply the medications that come later and then gently immobilize it."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes into the air, and are the two parts dislocated, it is necessary to align them evenly before an ulcer comes; and if a hot ulcer comes, let it remain some days until the ulcer is pacified; then set it evenly at the move that you can do lightly and surely, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than those with pieces; then hold it as it should be done hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces of bone broken, and they are separated into two parts, if it is the hand or foot, or use your hand if it is a small member, or with two ropes, or one rope and your hand; and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are disunited, then join by all means the additions in their places at the move that you can do, and ensure that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and fit together well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"And you can feel with your hand whether it is well aligned or not: if not, realign it carefully and do not immobilize too tightly nor press in such a way that heat and stiffness are caused in the limb due to poor technique, as we have said many times before."
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, then caution the patient well that he does not move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and ensure that the limb is so secured that it feels no pain.
