Then take the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and hip, and tie them together with three splints that are above, then return down to the bottom end of the thread until you reach the foot, and tie it so that it does not move from its place. Then leave it like that until no inflammation or other sign appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if inflammation occurs, remove the bandages and treat what has appeared, as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone that stick out, it is necessary to remove them if possible; and if not, it is necessary to cut open the space and draw out pus; then continue treatment until the patient is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone is fractured in such a way that rollers are applied to it, as in the case of the elbow and arm; however, with this type of treatment, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is healed in about one month or a little less or more, depending on the variety of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Ligamentous injury of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it is no more than a crack or hole, and this happens to every wound, and without wound, which everyone feels.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is to align what has shifted on its sides until it is assembled as much as possible, then apply plaster and place a round roller if necessary, and tighten as needed, then follow all the procedures that we have said for other fractures, such as heat inflammation and other signs; treat each situation with what is appropriate until healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Fractures of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is rightly called «mustelz», and the other «foscile». And there can be complete breaking like in the arm, and for this reason, the setting is similar to that of the arm, and the work is all done. And if the two bones break together, then the leg twists in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fibula is broken, turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, great pain is felt and it is clearly visible; it also turns under itself
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore arrange for an extension and place it evenly, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly and there are many pieces, then the extension should be lesser and lighter; and lighten according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"After completing your task, take two strips of wood and wrap them around the leg on both sides, from the knee downwards. Then wrap two layers of bandage over and under these strips, tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left. This is well done. Some people also use a splint made of wood the length of the leg to prevent movement, especially if there is an open wound at the fracture site. Move the leg every day to check for any signs of heat, infection, or other complications. Continue this care until it is fully healed."
de la brisure des os dou piet	"Of the fracture of the bones of the foot"
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	To the ankle there is no fracture,
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	"And if there is fracture of the foot bones, and you see these bones projecting over one another, then place that patient's foot on the ground, as if they were about to walk, and then place your foot upon theirs where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then apply a splint and bandages, and place beneath the stomach of the foot a small table with two heads, then bind it securely, and wrap it with cloths and other necessary items."
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	"And when three or four days have passed, undo the bandages, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they were broken or dislocated."
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	"And if there are any broken toes, set them straight as we have said for the fingers of the hand. Then place a splint along the length of the broken toe and make it slightly wider; then place beneath the foot that small table which I mentioned earlier, and bind it securely. If two or three, or more than three, toes are broken, then place on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and secure the table underneath the foot; let them be placed upon the top of the table so that they may support the arch of the foot."
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	"And remember not to forget the other things that I have mentioned for other fractures, and treat each case according to what is appropriate."
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	"Regarding the fracture of the wrist bone"
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, make her sit wide-legged, then lean her towards the back part, and have her held from behind. Then fill the space in her nature with cotton, as much as one stone. Then stand up the woman, lifting her back bit by bit, until the cotton comes to the entrance of her nature, and the bone returns with the stone. And when she wishes to piss, remove the cotton, and once she has pissed, replace it. Do this for about seven days: thus the break will be restored. If you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a tube at its opening, and put the whole bladder inside her nature. Then blow into the tube forcefully until the bladder swells within. Her nature will then return to normal. Then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for some days until she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the thigh; and these breaks are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice here, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break indicates many ways to correctly restore it: listen therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	"When the penis is broken, take a goose neck and insert it into the penis. Then wrap cloths around it and leave it like this for three days or thereabouts, and it will heal quickly."
de brisure avec plaie	"Regarding fractures with wounds"
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	He who has a fracture with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, should have his wound cleaned immediately, so that the stitches we have mentioned may testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then apply a dressing of vitriol, if you have none other, and then begin to reset the fracture in the same hour or on the same day, unless some obstacle arises.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if some obstacle arises, then leave the reduction until a new day, until the inflammation is subdued, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, lest you bring on an evil complication.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears above the exposed heart, it is necessary that you place it at ease quickly with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not sufficient for you to place it evenly with your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which is twenty or twenty-eight inches long and has a width according to the size of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the surgeon to take three or four, depending on what is needed in each case of fracture; and let it be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your operation, and let it be pointed at the front and thicker in the middle forward like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," therefore the curved head should be placed on the visible bone end; and push once until it returns, ensuring they are even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and tools cannot grip the bone well, then you must cut off the head of the bone until tools can grasp it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back together as we have said, then use a suitable instrument such as the incision knife or the bone cutter with all your strength; then reset that which remains in the bone by scraping off its roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset but the patient still feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So ensure it is in its proper place, then moisten a cloth with black stiptic wine and apply it if it is summer; do not put cerote or other oily substances on the wound, as this will cause rotting. Then apply bandages once you have reset the bone, leave the wound open, and cut away the skin around it according to the size of the wound. Be careful that the wound does not become constricted with the fracture; many foolish doctors have done this and caused harm or death to patients. Let the bandage be softer and gentler than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that ill will come of it, as we have said, and you find pain in that place, then one must not put on bandages; but wrap around tightly with hard cloths instead.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after two or three days that the wound is healing, then remove what you had put on previously and apply healing ointment to it, such as tetraformacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dress the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is sound and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the bowels can pass downward easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it still cannot heal but the bowels become obstructed again, know that there are small bone fragments causing this pain. Therefore, you must open the wound with a tent, and remove all these unwanted fragments that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears in the place, or another type of corruption, then you must treat it according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens up on the limb, such as the thighbone or armbone, and other similar ones in large limbs, then do not pull it out, for many die from this. But let it rot until after twenty or thirty days, perhaps it will fall out by itself later. Then treat the wound if you can; but if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	And of fractures that come upon the union
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times fractures come upon the union after it has healed, especially when they are near the joint, and it is an ugly sight to see the figure of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural movements.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore beware if the nail is fresh: you must administer stypptic medicines such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, sarcocolle, aconite, and similar others. So take some of these things or all together, and mix them with stypptic wine or with egg yolk or with axle grease; then put them on the nail in poultices and bind it tightly, and do not untie it for many days; then remove it and begin another one until the nodule is removed. Or you may bind a well-made piece of lead upon it, for the property of lead is to draw out all swellings from the limbs. And if the nodule has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut it open on top and remove the excess that appears. Or have it removed by some barber until it is gone, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone has been reset and afterward the limb remains weak and feeble, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been. Or because there were too many bindings, and nourishment could not reach the limb. Or because of too much restraining. Or because of too great movements, not at the proper time. Or because there is little blood in the body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the sick person eat well and exercise his body until blood increases in him. And administer baths, and give him joy and happiness. Then put pitch on the limb so that it attracts great nourishment to it, and apply warm water compresses often until nourishment reaches the limb, and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of the limb that is crooked after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration,
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And arrange gentle movement of the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	"And if the tortuosity is worn out and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed by iron, then one must cut all the way down to the bone with a fine, light-bladed scalpel. And use caution and skill in this procedure."
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	"Here begins the book of dislocations."
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	"Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its proper place, preventing it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient."
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	"If dislocation occurs in anyone, it must be immediately reduced without delay."
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	But if one delays, the place swells and perhaps will not be reset properly. Therefore, it is not good to move it while it is swollen: many times it brings about spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient bleed, then leave him until the inflammation has subsided; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each limb as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	"And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot."
des mandibules	"of the jawbone(s)"
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	"It sometimes happens that the jawbones are dislocated inward, and their dislocations occur in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their proper place and softened somewhat; or else they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chin, causing saliva to flow out of the mouth so that it cannot be held in, nor can the mouth be closed, and the tongue becomes entwined with speech."
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	"If the dislocation is slight, it returns on its own through various manipulations."
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must quickly reset it without delay; and in such a manner that the assistants hold the head of the patient, and the master places his clenched fist from one hand at the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and let the other two hands be free to press evenly; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	"And the doctor places it back into its proper place until it returns."
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	"And if the dislocation returns suddenly, especially if both jawbones have been dislocated together, then bathe them in warm water and oil until they can be gently manipulated without delay, as we have said."
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well without softening, then place moistened cloths made from a mixture of rose oil and wax on top, then bind it lightly with soft linen; and let the patient sleep on their back, with both shoulders supported between two pillows so that they do not move either to the right or left, nor try to chew, but take only light food until the pains are gone and the jaws are healed. Then he may eat what he wants easily, and need not strain himself opening his mouth for eating and drinking until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	"And if the two jawbones cannot be properly reduced within an hour and are not returned to their proper place, then fever and chills will ensue, sometimes with diarrhea, and occasionally with vomiting of bile."
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	"And when you see these symptoms, know that it is a loss [of life]; for many people who suffer from them die within eight days."
de la forcelle	"of dislocation of the jawbone at the angle"
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	"The angle [of the jaw] cannot be dislocated towards the cheek from within and from below the chin, but sometimes it can be dislocated backwards, which is easily felt."
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient should often lie on their back and extend their arms; then press firmly with your palm, and it will return to its place. Then place the emplastrum and bandage there, and bind it tightly; and the shoulder towards the side cannot dislocate again; if it does, reset it as we have said; then replace the emplastrum and bandage, and bind it tightly, and tell the patient to rest until they are healed. The same is done for the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	"of dislocation of the shoulder blade"
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder dislocates only in three ways: one is that it dislocates towards the lower part of the hip; and the second is towards the breastbone; and rarely dislocates upwards, which happens little; and it does not dislocate backwards due to the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inwardly for the nerves; and often dislocates downward towards the hip, especially those who have little flesh, as it quickly jumps out; while those with enough flesh hardly jump out and rarely return.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	"Sometimes, however, some men suffer a blow or a fracture and the shoulder becomes inflamed with heat, causing them to believe that it has been dislocated."
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	"It is therefore necessary for you to examine him until you are certain [of the diagnosis]; and then begin the treatment."
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations are recognized when they occur downwards towards the hip, and there is a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, which you will find clearly manifested between them; and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and below the hip where you touch the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their side nor move in any way; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly by touching it; and this manner of dislocation is difficult to reduce, especially when it is recent or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	"The method is for the practitioner to lift the patient's hand upwards, then place his fingers below the glenoid cavity and forcefully elevate the joint upwards into its proper place while the practitioner lifts the arm and extends it upwards; it will slip back quickly."
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within several days after, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and the plaster applied should be softening and soothing, like a decoction of marshmallow, fennel seed, and melilot in water, and the plaster applied. Then the patient should lie on their back, and place underneath the shoulder blade an even pillow made of wool, not too soft or too hard. The surgeon then places his heel on the pillow and gently lifts the head of the shoulder joint, pulling the patient's arm; another assistant holds the patient's head so that it does not move downwards. When this shoulder is now fully relocated, you should check if you have reset it correctly following this method: Ensure that there is a man present who is taller than the patient. He should stand directly facing the side, and place his shoulder underneath the patient's shoulder blade, lifting the shoulder blade upwards so that the patient hangs from the arm; another assistant pulls the patient's arm downwards towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, hang some heavy object with him, and the dislocation will return.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reset is also done in another way: and one takes a long stick and sticks it into the ground, such that its head is as high as a man's fist, but not too thick or too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but with soft cloths underneath, and the patient stands on the long end of the wood; then their hand is extended downwards on the other side properly, and the joint will quickly return to its place. And if it does not want to return despite all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick two spans wide and four fingers thick, which has a round head for easy insertion deep into the ass's tail, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie cloths under the head of the stick so that the stick does not hurt the patient; then place it under the armpit of the patient; and extend his arm along the length of the stick, and tie the sling to the stick, and the bandage at the top of the hand, then place the arm on one end of a board of similar width, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging down on the other side: the joint will now return.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, however it may be, then place under the armpit a wisp of wool; then put on the emplaster made with flour powder, with incense and egg yolk all around the shoulder, then wrap it tightly under the armpit, and twist the bandage onto the plaster, and bind the hand to its collar, and let the hand remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he should eat little until the member is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and afterwards he may eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has been forced out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for some other reason, then you must administer cauteries with three openings, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and after twenty days the joint does not stay in place, and he cannot raise his arm upwards, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut, stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the breast and nipples, or behind, is caused by a push or stretching of the hands, and another bandage should be applied; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there comes pain in the member and slowness of movement, then the patient should often apply hot compresses until that pain is alleviated and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	About dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the elbow joint is dislocated inwards and returns inwards, and it is dislocated from all sides, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not concealed because one can see and feel it well, and it is dislocated according to each type of figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick shoulder with the healthy one, so you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder completely
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you should reduce it before an abscess forms there, for if an abscess forms, it will be difficult to reduce, and perhaps it cannot be completely reduced, especially when it is behind; such dislocations are worse than others and cause greater pain, and sometimes gangrene occurs.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the reduction is when it can be reduced in such a way that you extend his hand with both your hands; and spread his arm, and place your hands on the elbow from above, below and around, and press the joint against the wrist or the root of the palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he folds his hand towards his hand and presses the elbow that is dislocated against the root of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and indeed two assistants extend the arm, and hold it steady with two hands so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm on each side, then when you have wrapped a doubled cloth long and wide around it; and when the physician has joined the joint in his hand, then he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then pushes the joint forcibly until it returns; and when it is in its place, then put a dry bandage on with egg yolk, and bind it firmly, and suspend the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it there for several days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, then untie the bandage and leave it. And if you see that the joint is not quite firm, then start again with the plaster and the bandage, leaving it on for several days until it is well secured, then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it feels cramped after the joint is reset and it moves, then bathe it and rub it gently, and press until it becomes relaxed; or you put on the joint a poultice of fatty mutton, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, if you rub the joint moderately, then replace the poultice, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see that, then put on a warm moist compress of wheat flour with butter, and bind it on; so it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	hand dislocations
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint is easily dislocated and its reduction is also easy compared to other joints. Therefore it must be reduced as soon as possible, before the place becomes swollen or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is thus: you place the sick hand on a table, and the servant extends it, and the physician places his hand over it evenly, so that he places his palm upon the joint's surface, and presses until it returns to its original position. Then you must ensure that it is properly in place; afterward, the patient places the back of their hand on a table for extension and reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient places their backhand on the table, and the physician places his hand over its joint surface.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that's good. If not, then apply plasters with soothing poultices until it rests without beginning again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot tolerate it, and you cannot set it right after several days, then the joint remains dislocated; causing no further harm to the patient unless the hand becomes lame and unable to grasp anything. Then know that the nerves or arteries are cut. There is no other cure but to cauterize nearby with a hot iron, and sometimes nothing else helps.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	"And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then untie it and let it remain so."
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, then apply warm water and rub until it is smooth."
de la dislocation des dois de la main	"Regarding the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The fingers of the hand are dislocated at each joint, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the wrist; therefore, reduce the dislocation towards your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the finger and tilt it towards the side where it is dislocated; leave it for two days, then make it even on that day; and on the third day, tie it with a splint as we have described, and on the fourth day, remove the splint and move it, and reapply the splint; do this frequently until it becomes stable. Do likewise if it is dislocated at the wrist of the hand, doing so until it is healed. And do similarly when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	"Regarding the dislocation of the heel bone of the back"
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	"When the heel bone of the foot or leg is dislocated, or when there are multiple dislocations, there is no treatment for this, as the damage is already done."
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the evacuations come out unwillingly and cannot be held back, and many times some member becomes limp, such as both thighs or both arms, or it moves in four parts; that which moves at the rear is called "gilbositez": its cure is that if gilbositez has come from childhood, then there is no cure nor healing for it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or impact or similar causes, the ancient ones prescribed remedies with great words, but not all were beneficial. However, I have summarized it according to my intention and formed tools in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the condition called 'gilbositeit' which affects the front of the chest, none has any healing. And likewise that which comes directly to both sides, and only one who knows properly can cure it when it comes to the back; as I say. And let the patient be laid down evenly on his face, with something underneath him so he does not bruise himself. Then stick one stake at the head firmly into the ground, and another at the feet, and bind a rope around the ankles of the patient, another at the hips, knees, and ankles; and two assistants should hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes. Let them be well secured, as we have said, and the physician place his palms firmly on the spine until it yields.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board of three long arms, and place it under the skin, and have the patient lie on their side, and put the head of the board under the skin, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the physician put his feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place. And if you wish, do this for the turned one that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you plant two stakes at the head of the patient's arm, one large and two smaller ones towards the feet, and between each stake, above and below, there should be a span of space; and in each stake there should be a hole where the dislocation occurs, and the stakes should be firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move. And between each pair of stakes there should be one turning stake on which the linen bandage turns, and two small stakes of one span long for turning the dislocation. Then tie the bandage that is among the stakes to the dislocation towards the head, and the other bandage towards the feet at the other dislocation, and each minister should turn his stake with all the bandages, and the master shall make the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, place a dry plaster with plenty of egg, then the lint, then the iron bar of three fingers' length, which holds down the place of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nourishment until they are healed; and if anything comes at the end of the healing, then administer softening and soothing medicines with the iron bar that we mentioned before; sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back spine of the back, and one thinks it is dislocation; but this is the bone that appears, therefore one should not be presumptuous: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	"Dislocations of the hip joint"
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	"Know that the hip and shoulder joints only have dislocations, unlike other joints. The hip joint is unstable in four ways: internally and externally, and anteriorly and posteriorly. It is more unstable internally than elsewhere, and somewhat less stable anteriorly and posteriorly."
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the sign of its dislocation within is that when one joins the patient's leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee opens more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee in the fire; and the place that is nearby swollen with a hot abscess is because the hip bone has come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	"And the sign of external hip dislocation is that these accidents are opposite to those mentioned earlier."
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	"And the sign of anterior hip dislocation is that the leg appears well-formed, but the knee cannot be bent without pain. If one tries to make the person walk, they cannot do so and hold back their urine. The ankle swells, and when they walk, they limp on the heel."
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	"And the sign of posterior hip dislocation is that the knee cannot be extended or bent, and the leg appears shorter than the other one. The ankle is relaxed, and the thighbone is located below the ribs."
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	"The treatment for this condition resembling hip dislocation is to examine whether the dislocation is old or new. If it is old and has healed in its displaced position, then there is no treatment for it. One should not attempt to reduce such a dislocation, as doing so could cause harm."
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	"For those hip dislocations that are fresh and occur in four ways (internal, external, anterior, and posterior), one should quickly reduce the dislocation using traction either internally or externally, and then move it to the right or left. If reduced correctly, no further treatment is necessary."
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong helper, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or one helper who is bound above the knee; and another helper extends his hand over it in such a way that he places his hands under the buttocks, then pulls him gently by a soft rope attached to the hip; and another helper holds the head of the rope; and all extend simultaneously up and down until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common for four members, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	But if not, then you must treat its appearance when the dislocation is at the shoulder, so that you raise the patient onto his healthy side, then place the rope on the root of the hip, and the place below the angle, then pull the rope upwards towards the angle, and towards the forearm; then another helper takes his arms, embraces the large bone of the sick hip, and extends it forcefully outwards: now it will return to its place. And this manner of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tie it in the manner that we have described, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a soft strong bond on both heels and knees, and let the affected leg extend two spans more than the other; then hang him from the top of a pole, and let him be two arm-lengths above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let another minister hang with the patient, embracing firmly the hip, for now the joint returns swiftly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the thigh, then let the patient lie down as we have described for one with gout, and bind the rope tightly on the affected leg properly and also on the foot; then place two brands, one at the head and one at the feet, and then drive a brand between the thighs of the patient in this manner; and have moist rags ready around so that the patient does not blister, then each minister extend towards him, and the doctor put his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place a stone on it, and press it as we have said in the chapter on gibbosity (kyphosis), with the patient lying on the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	"And when the dislocation is anterior, then one must extend the affected leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and let the physician place his pain on the affected angle of the hip, then press with the other hand, extending towards the knee."
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it is not necessary to extend the patient downwards or lift them up from the ground. Rather, they should lie as if the hip were dislocated at the front, just like we have described in childbirth over two hips; and they should be on their back, with the linen spread out as we have said earlier, and the joint should be pressed upon the table. And it will be ready when the patient extends their legs and they are even; then join the thighs together, place the splint, and tie it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let them rest for three or four days, then untie it and replace the splint on it. If you see that they are even, then tie it as before, and leave it for three days. Then untie it, and let them go gradually until the member is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	"The kneecap can be dislocated in three ways: inside and outside, and behind; it does not dislocate in front."
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend their leg at their hip, and if it does not articulate with their hip, know that it is dislocated. And the reduction of this [dislocation] is that you make the patient sit upright, extend their leg if they can, place your back on their face, and put their foot on yours; then take their knee in your palms, draw it between your thighs, then strongly flex both sides of the knee; and another assistant extends their foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that the leg articulates lightly with the hip; and apply the plaster there, fix the leg to the hip, and keep them bound tightly for three or four days, then untie them; and the patient should not walk until the member is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not yet straight, then extend it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is straight.
de la dislocation dou talon	Dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	"The heel is sometimes twisted and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward."
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it tents forward at the part where it is dislocated; the reduction should be easy, and one should gently extend it with both hands when it is merely moved.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, then you should make the patient sit upright, and have your assistants pull on the leg above the ankle with both hands; then draw the foot towards yourself with your right hand twice, then with your left hand twice, then lift it up and gently place the foot back into its proper position. Do this twice as described, drawing and placing the foot; if it stays in place, that's good; but if not, start over again because it has moved out of place once more. And if it still cannot be put back in place like this, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their thighs, and wrap cloth around it so it doesn't injure the patient. Then have one assistant hold onto the thigh, and another extend the foot with both hands or bind it to the neck of the foot; then each assistant should pull evenly, and the stake should always be between the patient's thighs to hold them steady when you lift them up. Finally, the surgeon himself should gently put the dislocation back in place with his hands, while one assistant holds onto the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return to its proper position.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is complete, then place the plaster and bandages on top, apply pressure strongly, tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are behind the ankle joint so that the binding is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding loosens, then apply pressure; then remove it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if they walk before this time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if inflammation comes afterwards, then you must calm it as we have said elsewhere until it is healed."
des dois	about the elbows
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	"When the elbows are dislocated, they should be gently reduced without force, and this is an easy thing to do."
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any nut of the back of the foot, then you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on two boards so that they are completely upright, and place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press strongly with your foot until it returns to its place; and when it is even, and nothing opens anymore, then place under the sole of the foot a board with two legs, then apply pressure strongly, and leave it for three days, then remove it; and make them rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	About wounds and dislocations at the same time
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you wish to reset it, many times the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in its treatment unless you are wise in the art and have long used it, and are compassionate and cautious, not hasty; and at first use things that cool an inflamed boil, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of healing; but when there is hope, then reset the limb to its place before the hot boils come; and once the limb is in place, administer things that cool an inflamed boil, and dress the wound with drying ointments as it should be done; and if bones are broken or small bones dislocated, set them and do what we have said for simple fractures; and guard against fear entering your way, according to what I have said, for this avails you more according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and body.
Amen	Amen
